Talaq — Divorce
advanced
12 min
When Prior Judicial Rulings Prevent Li'an from Cutting Lineage
Explanation of five cases with distinction of prior rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between prior judicial rulings that prevent li'an from cutting lineage and those that do not, applying the Hanafi criterion from Imam Muhammad's response to 'Isa ibn Abban.

Core Idea
A prior judicial ruling on a matter not directly related to marriage rights prevents li'an from cutting lineage; rulings on marriage rights do not.

This lesson explores a critical nuance in Hanafi family law: when does a prior judicial ruling block the effect of li'an in cutting a child's lineage? Through five specific cases from Imam Muhammad's Al-Jami' al-Kabir, we learn that the nature of the prior ruling matters. A ruling on blood-money or clarifying a suspended divorce is incidental and does not prevent li'an, while a ruling on maintenance, dower, or revocation directly involves marriage rights and thus does prevent li'an. This distinction, confirmed in a letter from Muhammad al-Shaybani to 'Isa ibn Abban, reveals the sophisticated interplay between judicial finality and the institution of li'an.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five cases
List the five cases from Al-Jami' al-Kabir as presented: two from Kitab al-Shahadat and one from Kitab al-Ma'aqil, and three from Kitab al-Da'wa. For each, note the initial judicial ruling.
Cases 1 and 2 involve blood-money and suspended divorce clarification; cases 3-5 involve maintenance, dower, and revocation.
2
Classify the rulings
Determine whether each prior ruling touches a 'right of marriage' (haqq al-nikah). Cases 1 and 2 are on matters not directly marriage rights; cases 3-5 are on marriage-related rights (maintenance, dower, revocation).
This classification is the key to the Hanafi distinction.
3
Apply the principle
Use Muhammad al-Shaybani's criterion: if the prior ruling was 'by necessity of a judgment on a matter not among the rights of marriage,' li'an does not cut lineage (cases 1 and 2). If the prior ruling was directly on a marriage right, li'an does cut lineage (cases 3-5).
This is found in the passage where Muhammad responds to 'Isa ibn Abban.
4
Consider the cross-madhhab perspective
Contrast the Hanafi position with the Shafi'i view that li'an always cuts lineage when performed, regardless of prior rulings. Note the practical difference in outcome.
The disagreement stems from different weights given to judicial finality versus the husband's right to deny paternity.

نسبه يلاعن القاضي بينهما ولا يقطع نسب الولد منه لأن القضاء بالديه على عاقلة الأب قضاء بكون الولد منه فلا ينقطع النسب بعده الثانية في الزيادات إذا قال لامرأتيه وقد دخل بهما إحداكما طالق ثلاثاً ولم يبين حتى ولدت إحداهما لأكثر من سنتين من وقت الطلاق كانت الولادة بياناً لوقوعه على الأخرى لأن الولد حصل من علوق حادث بعد الطلاق وتعينت التي ولدت للنكاح، فإن نفى الولد لاعن القاضي بينهما ولا يقطع النسب لأن حكم الشرع بكون الولد بياناً حكم بكونه منه وبعد الحكم به لا ينقطع باللعان وثلاث مسائل في كتاب الدعوى : الأولى امرأة ولدت وزوجها غائب فقطمت ولدها وطلبت من القاضي أن يفرض لها النفقة وللولد برهنت ثم حضر الزوج ونفى الولد لاعن وقطع النسب مع أنه محكوم به حيث فرض القاضي نفقته الثانية لو أنكر الدخول بعدما ولدت ثبت النسب ووجب لها كمال المهر فلو نفاه يلا عن ويقطع النسب مع أنه محكوم به حين قضى لها بكمال المهر. الثالثة المطلقة طلاقاً رجعياً إذا ولدت لأكثر من سنتين تكون رجعة ولو نفاه لاعن وقطع نسبه مع أنه محكوم به . وقد حكي أن عيسى بن أبان كتب إلى محمد بن الحسن حين كان بالرقة يستفرقه بين المسألتين الأوليين وبين الثلاث فكتب محمد رحمه الله أنه متى حصل القضاء بالنسب ضرورة القضاء بأمر ليس من حقوق النكاح فإنه يمنع قطع النسب باللعان وتمامه في شرح تلخيص الجامع من باب شهادة الملاعنة بالولد ومن المواضع المانعة من قطع النسب أن يقذفها أجنبي بنفي الولد ويحده القاضي لها فإنه حكم منه بثبوت نسبه فإذا نفاه بعده أبوه لا ينتفي كما في فتح القدير وسيأتي عن الذخيرة. ثم إذا قطع النسب عن الأب وألحق الولد بالأم يبقى النسب في حق سائر الأحكام من الشهادة والزكاة وعدم القصاص على الأب بقتله ونحو ذلك من الاقتصار على ما نقله قوله : (وقد ذكر الإمام محمد في الجامع الخ ظاهره أن هذا من كلام البدائع ولم أجده فيها، والذي رأيته بعد ذكره هذا الشرط السادس ما نصه وصورته ما روي عن أبي يوسف أنه قال في رجل جاءت امرأته بولد فنفاه ولم يلا عن حتى قذفها أجنبي بالولد الذي جاءت به فضرب القاضي الأجنبي الحد، فإن نسب الولد يثبت من الزوج فيسقط اللعان لأن القاضي لما حد قاذفها بالولد فقد حكم بكذبه والحكم بكذبه حكم بثبوت نسب الولد والنسب المحكوم بثبوته لا يحتمل النفي باللعان كالنسب المقر به، وإنما سقط اللعان لأن الحاكم لما حد قاذفها فقد حكم بإحصانها في عين ما قذفت به (۱) فلا يظهر في حق سائر الأحكام ا هـ. ويزاد السابع أن يكون النكاح صحيحاً فلا لعان بالقذف بنفي الولد في النكاح الفاسد والوطء بشبهة ولا ينتفي النسب. وقيد بالزوجية لأنه لو نفى نسب ولد أم الولد فإنه ينتفي بمجرد قوله بلا لعان. ويزاد الثامن أن يكون العلوق في حال يجري فيه اللعان حتى لو علق وهي كافرة لا ينتفي . وفي شهادات الجامع : ولدت توأمين فنفاهما ومات أحدهما عن أمه وأخيه وأخ منها فالسدس لها والثلث لهما والباقي يرد كأولاد العاهرة لانقطاع النسب وفيها اختلاف يعرف في موضعه ا هـ. وفي تتمة الفتاوى من الفرائض: ولد الملاعنة وولد الزنا في حكم الميراث بمنزلة ولد رشيدة ليس له أب ولا قرابة أب فلا يرث هذا الولد من الأب وقرابته ولا يرث الأب ولا قرابته من هذا الولد لأن قوم الأب تبع له في قطع النسب وهو ولد الأم فيرث منها ومن قرابتها وترث الأم وقرابتها وأما ابن ابن الملاعنة فله أب وقوم الأب وهم الإخوة وليس له جد صحيح ولا قومه مه وهم الأعمام والعمات لأب وأم أو لأب فإذا ثبت حرمة المصاهرة بين الزوجين ثم حدث بينهما ولد ثم مات الأب اختلفوا في ميراث هذا الولد منه للاختلاف في هذه الحرمة فلم يكن كولد الزنا كما لو جاءت بولد بعد النكاح المعلق طلاقها به فإن النسب فيه ثابت للاختلاف . ا هـ باختصار. وفي تلخيص الجامع : لو ملك النافي الأم لا يجوز بيعها. وفي شرحه وصورته رجل نفى نسب ولد امرأته الحرة ولاعن القاضي بينهما وقطع نسب الولد ثم ارتدت والعياذ بالله تعالى عن الإسلام ثم سبيت وملكها الزوج النافي فإنه لا يجوز له بيعها لأن نسب الولد ثابت حكماً لقيام فراشها ولا تصح دعوة غير النافي لهذا الولد وإن صدقه الثاني، وتصح دعوة النافي مطلقاً ولو كان المنفي كبيراً جاحداً للنسب من النافي. وفي التتارخانية : ولا ينتفي من أحكام النسب من جهة الزوج
Imam Muhammad mentioned in Al-Jami' al-Kabir five issues: two issues in the Book of Testimonies from Al-Talkhis; one in the Book of Blood-Money: a woman gave birth to a child who rolled onto a nursing infant, killing it, and the judge imposed the blood-money on the father's 'aqila; then the father denied the child's lineage; the judge performs li'an between them but does not cut the lineage from him because the judgment of blood-money on the father's 'aqila is a judgment that the child is from him, so lineage is not cut thereafter. The second in Al-Ziyadat: if he said to his two wives with whom he had consummated, 'One of you is triply divorced' without specifying, until one gave birth after more than two years from the time of divorce, the birth is a clarification that the divorce fell on the other, because the child resulted from a conception after the divorce, and the one who gave birth is determined as the wife; if he denies the child, the judge performs li'an between them and does not cut the lineage because the legal ruling that the child is a clarification is a ruling that it is from him, and after the ruling it is not cut by li'an. And three issues in the Book of Claims: First, a woman gave birth while her husband was absent, she weaned her child, and asked the judge to impose maintenance for her and the child, and she proved it; then the husband came and denied the child; he performs li'an and cuts the lineage even though it was ruled upon when the judge imposed maintenance. Second, if he denied consummation after she gave birth, the lineage is established and she deserves the full dower; if he then denies, he performs li'an and cuts the lineage even though it was ruled upon when the judge gave her the full dower. Third, a woman divorced revocably: if she gives birth after more than two years, it is a revocation; if he denies, he performs li'an and cuts his lineage even though it was ruled upon. It is narrated that 'Isa ibn Abban wrote to Muhammad ibn al-Hasan while he was in al-Raqqa asking him to differentiate between the first two issues and the three; Muhammad wrote that whenever a judgment of lineage occurs by necessity of a judgment on a matter not among the rights of marriage, it prevents cutting lineage by li'an, and its completion is in the commentary of Talkhis al-Jami' from the chapter on testimony of the lianah about the child. Among the places that prevent cutting lineage is that an outsider accuses her of denying the child and the judge imposes the hadd punishment on him; that is a ruling of establishing his lineage, so if the father afterwards denies, it is not negated, as in Fath al-Qadir, and it will come from Al-Dhakhirah. Then, if the lineage is cut from the father and the child is attached to the mother, the lineage remains regarding other rulings such as testimony, zakat, and the non-execution of qisas against the father for killing him, and similar restrictions according to what he transmitted. His statement: 'Imam Muhammad mentioned in Al-Jami'...' outwardly this is from the words of Al-Bada'i', but I did not find it therein; rather what I saw after mentioned this sixth condition is its text: its form is what is narrated from Abu Yusuf that he said concerning a man whose wife brought a child, and he denied it without performing li'an until an outsider accused her of the child she brought, and the judge imposed the hadd on the outsider; then the child's lineage is established from the husband, and li'an falls because when the judge imposed hadd on the accuser, he ruled him a liar, and ruling him a liar is a ruling of establishing the child's lineage, and a lineage ruled established does not admit negation by li'an, like a lineage confessed to; li'an only falls because when the judge imposed hadd on the accuser, he ruled on her being muhsan in that particular accusation, so it does not appear regarding other rulings. And the seventh is added: that the marriage be valid; so there is no li'an for accusing of denying the child in an invalid marriage or doubtful intercourse, and the lineage is not negated. It is restricted by marriage because if he denies the lineage of his umm walad's child, it is negated by his mere statement without li'an. And the eighth is added: that the conception occur at a time when li'an is possible; so if the child was conceived while she was an infidel, it is not negated. In Shihadat al-Jami': A woman gave birth to twins, and he denied both, and one of them died leaving his mother, his brother, and a brother from her; so one-sixth is for her, one-third for them, and the remainder is returned like the children of a prostitute because the lineage is cut; and there is difference known in its place. In Takmilat al-Fatawa from the chapter of inheritance: The child of a lianah and the child of zina are, in the ruling of inheritance, like a child of a rashidah woman; he has no father nor father's relatives; so this child does not inherit from the father and his relatives, nor does the father or his relatives inherit from this child because the father's people follow him in cutting lineage; he is the child of the mother, so he inherits from her and her relatives, and the mother and her relatives inherit from him. As for the son's son of the lianah, he has a father and the father's people—they are the brothers—and he has no valid grandfather nor his people—they are the paternal uncles and aunts. So if the prohibition of marriage affinity is established between the spouses, then a child occurs between them, then the father dies, they differed about the inheritance of this child from him due to difference about this prohibition, so it is not like the child of zina, just as if she brought a child after a marriage whose divorce was suspended on it, the lineage is established due to difference. In Talkhis al-Jami': If the father who denied owns the mother, it is not permissible to sell her. In its commentary: Its form: a man denied the lineage of his free wife's child, and the judge performed li'an between them and cut the child's lineage; then she apostatized, then was captured, and the father who denied owned her; it is not permissible for him to sell her because the child's lineage is established legally due to the existence of her marital bed; and the claim of other than the denier for this child is not valid even if the second affirms him; and the claim of the denier is valid absolutely even if the denied child is an adult denying lineage from the denier. In Al-Tatarkhaniyya: And from the rulings of lineage, it is not negated from the side of the husband.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is a detailed legal analysis from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, discussing when the li'an procedure does NOT succeed in cutting the child's lineage from the father. The author presents five cases from Imam Muhammad's Al-Jami' al-Kabir, then adds more conditions. The core principle is: if a previous judicial ruling has implicitly or explicitly confirmed the child's paternity, subsequent li'an cannot negate it. The five cases are: (1) a judge imposes blood-money on the father's 'aqila for a child's act, confirming paternity; (2) a wife's birth after more than two years from a suspended divorce clarifies the divorce, and paternity is established; (3) a judge grants maintenance for the child in the husband's absence, confirming paternity; (4) the husband denies consummation after birth but the judge awards full dower, confirming paternity; (5) a revocably divorced woman's birth after two years constitutes revocation, confirming paternity. In the first two cases, li'an does not cut lineage; in the latter three, it does cut lineage even though paternity was previously ruled. The distinction, as explained by Muhammad al-Shaybani, is that in the first two, the prior judgment was a necessary consequence of a ruling on a matter not directly related to marriage rights (blood-money or divorce clarification), so the paternity ruling is incidental and does not prevent li'an from operating. In the latter three, the prior judgment directly addressed marriage rights (maintenance, dower, revocation), so the paternity ruling is stronger and preempts li'an. The author then adds a sixth scenario: if an outsider accuses the mother and is given hadd for qadhf, that judgment confirms paternity and prevents the father's li'an from cutting lineage. Then two more conditions: seventh, the marriage must be valid (sahih) — for invalid marriage or doubtful intercourse, li'an is not applicable and lineage is not negated; eighth, the conception must occur at a time when li'an is possible (e.g., not while the wife is an infidel). The passage also discusses inheritance consequences: a child of li'an or zina inherits only from the mother's side, not the father's. An example from inheritance law is given for a twin situation. The author also rules that if the father who denied later owns the mother (e.g., by captivity), he cannot sell her because the child's lineage is legally considered established despite the li'an, so she is an umm walad. This shows the complexity of Hanafi law: li'an cuts lineage for some purposes (inheritance, paternity rights) but not for others (sale of mother, some criminal matters).

Key Terms
اللعان (al-li‘ān): A mutual oath and imprecation between spouses when the husband accuses his wife of adultery or denies paternity, leading to divorce and permanent separation, and for the husband, the denial of the child's lineage.
النسب (al-nasab): Lineage or paternity; the legal relationship between a child and his father, entailing inheritance, custody, and other rights.
حقوق النكاح (huqūq al-nikāḥ): Rights of marriage; legal entitlements and obligations that arise from the marriage contract, such as maintenance, dower, and the status of marriage (including revocation).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, which of the following scenarios prevents the father from cutting lineage by li'an?
A) A judge imposes blood-money on the father's 'aqila for a child's accidental killing.
B) A judge grants maintenance for the child while the husband is absent.
C) A judge gives the wife full dower after the husband denies consummation.
D) A judge confirms revocation of divorce based on birth after two years.

Key Takeaway
A prior judicial ruling only prevents li'an from cutting lineage if it was made necessary by a matter not directly a right of marriage; if the ruling directly concerns a marriage right, li'an retains its full effect.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
Additional Conditions and Inheritance of the Li'an Child
Additional conditions from later authorities and inheritance rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sixth through eighth conditions that prevent li'an from cutting lineage, and calculate the inheritance distribution for a child of li'an who dies leaving a mother and uterine brothers.

Core Idea
Li'an's effect is blocked by hadd on an accuser, invalid marriage, or conception during the wife's apostasy; the child's inheritance is limited to the mother's side with radd.

Beyond the five cases from Al-Jami' al-Kabir, the Hanafi school adds further conditions that prevent li'an from cutting lineage. These include a prior hadd punishment on an outsider for qadhf, the requirement of a valid marriage at conception, and the condition that conception occurs during a period when li'an is possible. Additionally, the passage addresses inheritance: a child of li'an is treated like a foundling, inheriting only from the mother and her relatives, with the residue returned by radd. These rules complete the picture of how li'an interacts with other legal institutions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sixth condition (hadd on outsider)
From Abu Yusuf: if an outsider accuses the mother and receives hadd for qadhf, this ruling confirms paternity and prevents the husband's li'an from cutting lineage. Understand why this is analogous to the first two cases: the hadd ruling is on a matter not directly a marriage right.
This condition is added from Abu Yusuf, as cited in the passage.
2
Identify the seventh condition (valid marriage)
Li'an does not cut lineage if the marriage is invalid (fasid) or if intercourse was doubtful (shubha). In such cases, lineage is never cut; the child is attributed to the father via the marital bed presumption. This condition restricts the applicability of li'an.
The passage explicitly states: 'li'an in invalid marriage and doubtful intercourse' does not cut lineage.
3
Identify the eighth condition (conception time)
Li'an cannot cut lineage if the child was conceived while the wife was an infidel (i.e., before marriage or during a period of apostasy). This is because li'an is only applicable when there is a valid marriage at the time of conception.
The passage adds: 'until if the child was conceived while she was an infidel, it is not negated.'
4
Calculate inheritance for a child of li'an
Use the faraid panel: heirs are mother (1/6) and two uterine brothers (1/3 total). Since there is no father or paternal relatives, the residue is returned via radd. Calculate the final shares: mother gets 1/3, each brother gets 1/3.
The passage gives an example from Shihadat al-Jami' with twins.

رأيته بعد ذكره هذا الشرط السادس ما نصه وصورته ما روي عن أبي يوسف أنه قال في رجل جاءت امرأته بولد فنفاه ولم يلا عن حتى قذفها أجنبي بالولد الذي جاءت به فضرب القاضي الأجنبي الحد، فإن نسب الولد يثبت من الزوج فيسقط اللعان لأن القاضي لما حد قاذفها بالولد فقد حكم بكذبه والحكم بكذبه حكم بثبوت نسب الولد والنسب المحكوم بثبوته لا يحتمل النفي باللعان كالنسب المقر به، وإنما سقط اللعان لأن الحاكم لما حد قاذفها فقد حكم بإحصانها في عين ما قذفت به (۱) فلا يظهر في حق سائر الأحكام ا هـ. ويزاد السابع أن يكون النكاح صحيحاً فلا لعان بالقذف بنفي الولد في النكاح الفاسد والوطء بشبهة ولا ينتفي النسب. وقيد بالزوجية لأنه لو نفى نسب ولد أم الولد فإنه ينتفي بمجرد قوله بلا لعان. ويزاد الثامن أن يكون العلوق في حال يجري فيه اللعان حتى لو علق وهي كافرة لا ينتفي . وفي شهادات الجامع : ولدت توأمين فنفاهما ومات أحدهما عن أمه وأخيه وأخ منها فالسدس لها والثلث لهما والباقي يرد كأولاد العاهرة لانقطاع النسب وفيها اختلاف يعرف في موضعه ا هـ. وفي تتمة الفتاوى من الفرائض: ولد الملاعنة وولد الزنا في حكم الميراث بمنزلة ولد رشيدة ليس له أب ولا قرابة أب فلا يرث هذا الولد من الأب وقرابته ولا يرث الأب ولا قرابته من هذا الولد لأن قوم الأب تبع له في قطع النسب وهو ولد الأم فيرث منها ومن قرابتها وترث الأم وقرابتها وأما ابن ابن الملاعنة فله أب وقوم الأب وهم الإخوة وليس له جد صحيح ولا قومه مه وهم الأعمام والعمات لأب وأم أو لأب فإذا ثبت حرمة المصاهرة بين الزوجين ثم حدث بينهما ولد ثم مات الأب اختلفوا في ميراث هذا الولد منه للاختلاف في هذه الحرمة فلم يكن كولد الزنا كما لو جاءت بولد بعد النكاح المعلق طلاقها به فإن النسب فيه ثابت للاختلاف . ا هـ باختصار. وفي تلخيص الجامع : لو ملك النافي الأم لا يجوز بيعها. وفي شرحه وصورته رجل نفى نسب ولد امرأته الحرة ولاعن القاضي بينهما وقطع نسب الولد ثم ارتدت والعياذ بالله تعالى عن الإسلام ثم سبيت وملكها الزوج النافي فإنه لا يجوز له بيعها لأن نسب الولد ثابت حكماً لقيام فراشها ولا تصح دعوة غير النافي لهذا الولد وإن صدقه الثاني، وتصح دعوة النافي مطلقاً ولو كان المنفي كبيراً جاحداً للنسب من النافي. وفي التتارخانية : ولا ينتفي من أحكام النسب من جهة الزوج
Imam Muhammad mentioned in Al-Jami' al-Kabir five issues: two issues in the Book of Testimonies from Al-Talkhis; one in the Book of Blood-Money: a woman gave birth to a child who rolled onto a nursing infant, killing it, and the judge imposed the blood-money on the father's 'aqila; then the father denied the child's lineage; the judge performs li'an between them but does not cut the lineage from him because the judgment of blood-money on the father's 'aqila is a judgment that the child is from him, so lineage is not cut thereafter. The second in Al-Ziyadat: if he said to his two wives with whom he had consummated, 'One of you is triply divorced' without specifying, until one gave birth after more than two years from the time of divorce, the birth is a clarification that the divorce fell on the other, because the child resulted from a conception after the divorce, and the one who gave birth is determined as the wife; if he denies the child, the judge performs li'an between them and does not cut the lineage because the legal ruling that the child is a clarification is a ruling that it is from him, and after the ruling it is not cut by li'an. And three issues in the Book of Claims: First, a woman gave birth while her husband was absent, she weaned her child, and asked the judge to impose maintenance for her and the child, and she proved it; then the husband came and denied the child; he performs li'an and cuts the lineage even though it was ruled upon when the judge imposed maintenance. Second, if he denied consummation after she gave birth, the lineage is established and she deserves the full dower; if he then denies, he performs li'an and cuts the lineage even though it was ruled upon when the judge gave her the full dower. Third, a woman divorced revocably: if she gives birth after more than two years, it is a revocation; if he denies, he performs li'an and cuts his lineage even though it was ruled upon. It is narrated that 'Isa ibn Abban wrote to Muhammad ibn al-Hasan while he was in al-Raqqa asking him to differentiate between the first two issues and the three; Muhammad wrote that whenever a judgment of lineage occurs by necessity of a judgment on a matter not among the rights of marriage, it prevents cutting lineage by li'an, and its completion is in the commentary of Talkhis al-Jami' from the chapter on testimony of the lianah about the child. Among the places that prevent cutting lineage is that an outsider accuses her of denying the child and the judge imposes the hadd punishment on him; that is a ruling of establishing his lineage, so if the father afterwards denies, it is not negated, as in Fath al-Qadir, and it will come from Al-Dhakhirah. Then, if the lineage is cut from the father and the child is attached to the mother, the lineage remains regarding other rulings such as testimony, zakat, and the non-execution of qisas against the father for killing him, and similar restrictions according to what he transmitted. His statement: 'Imam Muhammad mentioned in Al-Jami'...' outwardly this is from the words of Al-Bada'i', but I did not find it therein; rather what I saw after mentioned this sixth condition is its text: its form is what is narrated from Abu Yusuf that he said concerning a man whose wife brought a child, and he denied it without performing li'an until an outsider accused her of the child she brought, and the judge imposed the hadd on the outsider; then the child's lineage is established from the husband, and li'an falls because when the judge imposed hadd on the accuser, he ruled him a liar, and ruling him a liar is a ruling of establishing the child's lineage, and a lineage ruled established does not admit negation by li'an, like a lineage confessed to; li'an only falls because when the judge imposed hadd on the accuser, he ruled on her being muhsan in that particular accusation, so it does not appear regarding other rulings. And the seventh is added: that the marriage be valid; so there is no li'an for accusing of denying the child in an invalid marriage or doubtful intercourse, and the lineage is not negated. It is restricted by marriage because if he denies the lineage of his umm walad's child, it is negated by his mere statement without li'an. And the eighth is added: that the conception occur at a time when li'an is possible; so if the child was conceived while she was an infidel, it is not negated. In Shihadat al-Jami': A woman gave birth to twins, and he denied both, and one of them died leaving his mother, his brother, and a brother from her; so one-sixth is for her, one-third for them, and the remainder is returned like the children of a prostitute because the lineage is cut; and there is difference known in its place. In Takmilat al-Fatawa from the chapter of inheritance: The child of a lianah and the child of zina are, in the ruling of inheritance, like a child of a rashidah woman; he has no father nor father's relatives; so this child does not inherit from the father and his relatives, nor does the father or his relatives inherit from this child because the father's people follow him in cutting lineage; he is the child of the mother, so he inherits from her and her relatives, and the mother and her relatives inherit from him. As for the son's son of the lianah, he has a father and the father's people—they are the brothers—and he has no valid grandfather nor his people—they are the paternal uncles and aunts. So if the prohibition of marriage affinity is established between the spouses, then a child occurs between them, then the father dies, they differed about the inheritance of this child from him due to difference about this prohibition, so it is not like the child of zina, just as if she brought a child after a marriage whose divorce was suspended on it, the lineage is established due to difference. In Talkhis al-Jami': If the father who denied owns the mother, it is not permissible to sell her. In its commentary: Its form: a man denied the lineage of his free wife's child, and the judge performed li'an between them and cut the child's lineage; then she apostatized, then was captured, and the father who denied owned her; it is not permissible for him to sell her because the child's lineage is established legally due to the existence of her marital bed; and the claim of other than the denier for this child is not valid even if the second affirms him; and the claim of the denier is valid absolutely even if the denied child is an adult denying lineage from the denier. In Al-Tatarkhaniyya: And from the rulings of lineage, it is not negated from the side of the husband.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is a detailed legal analysis from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, discussing when the li'an procedure does NOT succeed in cutting the child's lineage from the father. The author presents five cases from Imam Muhammad's Al-Jami' al-Kabir, then adds more conditions. The core principle is: if a previous judicial ruling has implicitly or explicitly confirmed the child's paternity, subsequent li'an cannot negate it. The five cases are: (1) a judge imposes blood-money on the father's 'aqila for a child's act, confirming paternity; (2) a wife's birth after more than two years from a suspended divorce clarifies the divorce, and paternity is established; (3) a judge grants maintenance for the child in the husband's absence, confirming paternity; (4) the husband denies consummation after birth but the judge awards full dower, confirming paternity; (5) a revocably divorced woman's birth after two years constitutes revocation, confirming paternity. In the first two cases, li'an does not cut lineage; in the latter three, it does cut lineage even though paternity was previously ruled. The distinction, as explained by Muhammad al-Shaybani, is that in the first two, the prior judgment was a necessary consequence of a ruling on a matter not directly related to marriage rights (blood-money or divorce clarification), so the paternity ruling is incidental and does not prevent li'an from operating. In the latter three, the prior judgment directly addressed marriage rights (maintenance, dower, revocation), so the paternity ruling is stronger and preempts li'an. The author then adds a sixth scenario: if an outsider accuses the mother and is given hadd for qadhf, that judgment confirms paternity and prevents the father's li'an from cutting lineage. Then two more conditions: seventh, the marriage must be valid (sahih) — for invalid marriage or doubtful intercourse, li'an is not applicable and lineage is not negated; eighth, the conception must occur at a time when li'an is possible (e.g., not while the wife is an infidel). The passage also discusses inheritance consequences: a child of li'an or zina inherits only from the mother's side, not the father's. An example from inheritance law is given for a twin situation. The author also rules that if the father who denied later owns the mother (e.g., by captivity), he cannot sell her because the child's lineage is legally considered established despite the li'an, so she is an umm walad. This shows the complexity of Hanafi law: li'an cuts lineage for some purposes (inheritance, paternity rights) but not for others (sale of mother, some criminal matters).

Key Terms
الحد (al-ḥadd): Fixed punishment prescribed by Shariah for certain crimes. Here, hadd for qadhf (false accusation of adultery) confirms the child's paternity.
الرجعة (al-raj‘a): Revocation of a revocable divorce; if the wife gives birth within the waiting period, it is a sign of revocation.
الرد (al-radd): Return of surplus inheritance to Quranic heirs in proportion to their shares, when there is no asabah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the additional conditions in this passage, which of the following scenarios would prevent li'an from cutting lineage?
A) The marriage was valid and the conception occurred while the wife was Muslim.
B) An outsider was given hadd for accusing the wife of adultery regarding the child.
C) The marriage was fasid (invalid) at the time of conception.
D) The husband performed li'an before any judicial ruling.

Key Takeaway
Li'an is a powerful tool for denying paternity, but its effect is limited by prior adjudications, the validity of marriage, and the timing of conception; inheritance consequences follow the rule that the child has no father.

The Limited Effect of Li'an: Only Inheritance and Maintenance Are Negated
Ruling on the limited effect of li'an and addition of two conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the limited effect of li'an on negating paternity and explain the two additional conditions required for negation.

Core Idea
Li'an only negates inheritance and maintenance; other paternal rights remain because 'the child belongs to the marriage bed'.

This passage clarifies that when a husband denies paternity through li'an, the legal effect is not total. The hadith 'al-walad lil-firash' establishes the child's attribution to the marriage bed, so li'an only overrides this default for inheritance and maintenance. Additionally, the author adds two conditions for the negation to be effective: the marriage must be valid, and conception must occur at a time when li'an is applicable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default rule from the hadith
The hadith 'al-walad lil-firash' (the child belongs to the marriage bed) establishes that a child born to a married woman is attributed to her husband. This is the default ruling.
2
State the limited override caused by li'an
Li'an only overcomes this default for two specific effects: inheritance between father and child does not occur, and the father is not obligated to provide maintenance. All other rulings (e.g., prohibition of marriage between the child and the father's relatives) remain intact.
3
Explain the first condition: valid marriage
If the marriage is invalid (fasid) or conception occurs through intercourse by mistake (shubha), li'an is not valid and lineage is not negated.
This condition applies to the li'an procedure itself, not specifically to negation.
4
Explain the second condition: conception during li'an-applicable period
The child's conception must occur at a time when li'an is possible. For example, if the wife was an unbeliever at conception and later accepted Islam, li'an cannot be performed because the ground for li'an did not exist at the critical time.
Al-Hamawi considered these two as conditions of li'an, not of negation, but the practical effect is the same.
5
Note the judicial requirement for the judge's statement
Some scholars add that after the separation, the judge must explicitly state: 'I have cut the lineage of this child from him.' Mere separation is insufficient.
This is mentioned as a proper addition in the commentary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأحكام إلا أنه لا يجري التوارث بينهما، ولا نفقة على الأب لأن النفي باللعان ثبت شرعاً بخلاف الأصل بناء على زعمه وظنه مع كونه مولوداً على فراشه وقد قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم «الولد للفراش» فلا يظهر في حق سائر الأحكام ا هـ. ويزاد السابع أن يكون النكاح صحيحاً فلا لعان بالقذف بنفي الولد في النكاح الفاسد والوطء بشبهة ولا ينتفي النسب. وقيد بالزوجية لأنه لو نفى نسب ولد أم الولد فإنه ينتفي بمجرد قوله بلا لعان. ويزاد الثامن أن يكون العلوق في حال يجري فيه اللعان حتى لو علق وهي كافرة لا ينتفي . قوله : (ويزاد السابع (الخ قال الحموي : التحقيق أن هذا الشرط والذي بعده من شرائط اللعان لا من شرائط النفي فلذا حذفهما في البدائع .اهـ. وأصله لصاحب النهر. وأقول : على أن الثامن يغني عن هذا السابع كما لا يخفى. وينبغي أن يزاد قول القاضي بعد التفريق قطعت نسب هذا الولد عنه على ما هو الصحيح كما يأتي
Rulings: except that inheritance does not occur between them, and there is no maintenance upon the father, because negation through li'an is established legally contrary to the original rule based on his claim and assumption while the child is born on his bed, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The child belongs to the marriage bed.' So it does not appear in regard to other rulings. End. And the seventh condition is added: that the marriage be valid, so there is no li'an by accusing of fornication to negate a child in an invalid marriage or intercourse by suspicion, and lineage is not negated. And it is restricted to marriage, because if he negates the lineage of a child of a slave-concubine (umm walad), it is negated by his mere statement without li'an. And the eighth condition is added: that the conception occur in a time in which li'an is applicable, such that if she conceived while she was an unbeliever, it is not negated. His statement: 'And the seventh is added etc.' al-Hamawi said: The verification is that this condition and the one after it are from the conditions of li'an, not from the conditions of negation, so they were omitted in al-Bada'i'. End. Its origin is from the author of al-Nahr. And I say: The eighth suffices for the seventh, as is not hidden. And it is proper to add the statement of the judge after separation: 'I have cut the lineage of this child from him' according to the correct view, as will come.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Prophet's hadith. It first explains that when a husband negates paternity through li'an, the legal effect is limited: inheritance between father and child does not occur, and the father is not obligated to provide maintenance. This is because the negation is based on the husband's claim, while the child is born on his marriage bed, and the hadith 'al-walad lil-firash' (the child belongs to the marriage bed) establishes the default attribution. Therefore, li'an overrides this default only for inheritance and maintenance, not for other rulings like prohibiting marriage between the child and the father's relatives. The author then adds two conditions for the negation to be effective: first, the marriage must be valid; in a fasid marriage or intercourse by shubha, li'an is not valid and lineage is not negated. Second, the conception must occur at a time when li'an is possible. For example, if the wife was an unbeliever at conception and later accepted Islam, li'an is not possible because the ground for li'an did not exist at the critical time. The commentary notes that al-Hamawi considered these to be conditions of li'an itself, not of negation, and that the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq thinks the eighth condition makes the seventh redundant. He also suggests adding that the judge must explicitly state 'I have cut the lineage of this child from him' after separating the spouses, otherwise the mere separation does not suffice for negation.

Key Terms
لعان (liʿān): Mutual imprecation between spouses where the husband accuses the wife of adultery or denies paternity of her child, and the wife swears to defend herself.
الفراش (al-firāsh): The marriage bed; the legal basis for attributing a child to the husband.
نفي الولد (nafī al-walad): The act of denying paternity of a child through li'an.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a legal effect of a valid li'an on the father-child relationship according to this passage?
A) Inheritance between father and child is cut.
B) The father's obligation to provide maintenance is removed.
C) The child becomes a non-mahram for the father (marriage becomes permissible).
D) The child continues to be considered the father's child for other rulings.

Key Takeaway
Li'an only negates inheritance and maintenance; the father-child relationship remains intact for all other legal rulings due to the default attribution from the hadith 'al-walad lil-firash'.

Li'an for Eunuch or Castrated Man: A Hanafi Dispute
Critical refinement of a ruling on li'an

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on li'an for a eunuch or castrated man and explain the rationale behind each.

Core Idea
A castrated man may still father a child through friction, making li'an possible to deny lineage.

Li'an is a procedure where a husband denies paternity under oath. But what if the husband is physically incapable of fathering a child? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a disagreement: al-Dhakhira says li'an is not valid for eunuchs or castrated men, but the author, Ibn Nujaym, questions this by pointing out that even a castrated man can ejaculate through mechanical stimulation, making paternity possible. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial ruling
Read the quote from al-Dhakhira: li'an is not legislated for a eunuch (khasi) or a castrated man (majbub) to deny a child. The reason given: a child cannot be attributed to such a man.
2
Understand the underlying principle
Li'an is a last resort when the husband denies a child that could be his. If biology makes fatherhood impossible, there is no need for li'an—the child simply is not his. This is the logic of al-Dhakhira.
3
Analyze the objection
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq says 'there is consideration' (fīhi naẓar). He argues that a majbub can ejaculate through grinding (saḥq), so it is possible for a child to be attributed to him. Therefore, li'an may still be needed to deny paternity.
The key is the possibility of ejaculation, not the presence of genitals.
4
Determine the practical consequence
If the husband can produce semen, even by unconventional means, then the child could be his, so li'an is valid. This shifts the focus from physical anatomy to functional capability.
5
Note the authority level
Al-Dhakhira's ruling is earlier, but Ibn Nujaym is a later authoritative commentator. The passage does not decisively choose, but the objection opens the door for a wider application of li'an.
In fatwa, later Hanafi scholars often consider the possibility of impregnation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وفي الذخيرة لا يشرع اللعان بنفي الولد في الخصي والمجبوب الخ) لأنه لا يلحق به الولد ؛ كذا في الفتح عن الذخيرة. ثم قال : وفيه نظر لأن المجبوب ينزل بالسحق ويثبت نسب ولده
His statement: (And in al-Dhakhira: Li'an by negation of a child is not legislated for the eunuch and the castrated man, etc.) because the child is not attributed to him; thus in al-Fath from al-Dhakhira. Then he said: There is consideration in it, because the castrated man (majbub) can ejaculate through grinding (sahq), and the lineage of his child is established.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement by the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. He quotes al-Dhakhira's ruling that li'an is not valid for a eunuch (khasi) or a castrated/impotent man (majbub) to deny paternity of a child, because such a man cannot father a child, so there is no need for li'an. However, the author comments that this view is questionable. He argues that a majbub (castrated man who still has his penis and testicles removed? Actually, majbub typically means a man whose genitals have been removed, but he points out that even such a man can ejaculate through friction (sahq, i.e., grinding or rubbing), and thus a child could potentially be attributed to him. Therefore, li'an may still be needed to deny lineage. This shows a nuanced understanding of the physical possibilities. The final reliance on al-Dhakhira or this criticism? The author does not decisively choose, but he presents his objection. In practice, Hanafi fatwa might follow the view that li'an is possible if the husband can be a biological father, which may be the more widely accepted position. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
خصي (khaṣī): Eunuch; a male whose testicles are removed or are non-functional.
مجبوب (majbūb): A male whose genitals (penis and testicles) are removed or are non-functional.
سحق (saḥq): Grinding or rubbing, a means of ejaculation for a castrated man.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because a castrated man can still ejaculate through grinding, making paternity possible.
B) Because al-Dhakhira's text is considered weak.
C) Because the hadith on li'an explicitly includes castrated men.
D) Because the wife's consent is required.

Key Takeaway
The validity of li'an for a eunuch or castrated man hinges on the possibility of paternity; if ejaculation is possible, li'an is valid.

The Limited Effect of Li'an on Paternity
States that li'an only severs inheritance and maintenance, leaving all other paternal lineage rulings intact

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that li'an severs only inheritance and maintenance, and identify the conditions under which paternity negation does or does not occur.

Core Idea
Li'an severs only inheritance and maintenance; all other paternal lineage effects remain.

When a husband accuses his wife of zina and performs li'an, it is natural to assume that all father-child ties are cut. However, the Hanafi school holds a more nuanced view: only two legal consequences—inheritance and maintenance—are removed. All other rights and duties, such as guardianship and marriage prohibitions, persist. This lesson unpacks that principle through key cases from the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
State the General Ruling
Read the opening phrase: 'Except for inheritance and maintenance, all other rulings of lineage from the husband's side remain in effect.' This is the core Hanafi position.
The term 'jawānib' (جوانب) refers to all aspects of paternal lineage.
2
Analyze the Supporting Cases
Work through the examples from al-Dhakhira: paternity established by acknowledgment or court ruling cannot be negated later; li'an is ineffective when the couple is not eligible or does not perform the ritual.
The case of a slave or kitābiyya at conception shows that eligibility is a prerequisite for effective negation.
3
Distinguish Between Accusation and Negation
Note that merely calling the wife 'fornicator' does not negate paternity; explicit denial of the child is required. If the husband retracts, he is flogged.
This distinction is from al-Sighnaqi and prevents automatic paternity negation.
4
Apply the Principle
Consider a scenario: a husband performs li'an but does not explicitly deny the child. What is the effect? Based on the text, li'an is established but paternity is not negated.
The mufta bihi position is that only inheritance and maintenance are severed in such a case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سوي التوارث وإيجاب النفقة وما عداهما من أحكام النسب من جهة الزوج قائمة. وفي الذخيرة : وكل نسب ثبت بإقراره أو بطريق الحكم لم ينتف بعد ذلك وبيانه فيما روي عن أبي يوسف في رجل جاءت امرأته بولد فنفاه فلم يلاعنها حتى قذفها أجنبي بالولد فحد فقد ثبت نسب الولد ولا ينتفي بعد ذلك، ولو نفى ولد زوجته اللعان وهما مما لا لعان بينهما لا ينتفي، سواء وجب الحد أو لم يجب، وكذا إذا كانا من أهل اللعان ولم يتلاعنا فإنه لا ينتفي، وكذا إذا كان العلوق في حال لا لعان بينهما ثم صارا بحال يتلاعنان نحو إن كانت المرأة أمة أو كتابية حالة العلوق فأعتقت أو أسلمت فإنهما لا يتلاعنان ولا ينتفي نسب الولد. وفي السغناقي : ولو قال لامرأته يا زانية ولها ولد منه ثبت اللعان ولا يلزم نفي الولد فإن أكذب نفسه حده القاضي ا.هـ. ولذا قيد النفي بقذف الولد احترازاً عما إذا قذفها بالزنا ولها منه ولد فإنه لا ينتفي نسبه . ثم اعلم أن هذا الولد وإن قطع القاضي نسبه عن أبيه لم تصح دعوى أحد لنسبه وإن صدقة الولد كما في التتارخانية وهو مستفاد من قولهم إن قطع النسب لا يظهر إلا في مسألتين.
Except for inheritance and maintenance, all other rulings of lineage from the husband's side remain in effect. And in al-Dhakhira: Every lineage established by his acknowledgment or by way of judicial ruling cannot be negated afterwards. Its explanation is in what was narrated from Abu Yusuf regarding a man whose wife brought a child and he denied it, but he did not perform li'an until a stranger accused her of zina regarding the child and was flogged—then the child's lineage is established and cannot be negated afterwards. And if he denied the child of his wife through li'an while they are not eligible for li'an, it is not negated, whether the hadd becomes obligatory or not. Likewise, if they are eligible for li'an but did not perform li'an, it is not negated. Likewise, if the conception occurred in a state where no li'an is between them, then they came to a state where they could perform li'an, such as if the woman was a slave or a kitabiyya at the time of conception, then she was freed or became Muslim—then they do not perform li'an and the child's lineage is not negated. And in al-Sighnaqi: If he said to his wife 'O fornicator' while she has a child from him, li'an is established and negation of the child is not required. If he then retracts himself, the qadi flogs him. Hence, negation is restricted to accusing the child of zina, to exclude the case where he accuses her of zina and she has a child from him—then his lineage is not negated. Then know that this child, even if the qadi cuts off his lineage from his father, no one's claim to his lineage is valid, even if the child confirms it, as in al-Tatarkhaniyyah, and it is derived from their saying that cutting off lineage is only apparent in two cases.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, opening with a general principle and then listing cases to illustrate it. The general ruling is that when a husband accuses his wife of zina and performs li'an, the only legal effects that are severed between the child and the father are inheritance and maintenance. All other rights and duties arising from the paternal relationship remain intact. The text then provides evidential cases from al-Dhakhira: if paternity was established by the husband's admission or by a court ruling, it cannot be later negated by li'an. For instance, if a husband denies a child but fails to perform li'an, and then an outsider accuses the wife and is punished for qadhf, the child's paternity is confirmed. Additionally, if the couple is not eligible for li'an (e.g., if the wife was a slave or non-Muslim at conception) and the husband denies the child, the denial is ineffective. Even if they become eligible later (e.g., the wife is freed or converts), they still cannot perform li'an to negate the child. Al-Sighnaqi adds that if the husband merely calls his wife a fornicator without explicitly negating the child, li'an is established but negation of the child does not follow; if he retracts, he is flogged. The passage concludes that once a judge has decreed the negation of paternity, no one else—including the child himself—can later claim the child's lineage to the father.

Key Terms
اللعان (al-li‘ān): Mutual imprecation between spouses when the husband accuses his wife of zina without witnesses, involving oaths and curses.
نفي الولد (nafy al-walad): The husband's denial that a child born to his wife is his own, typically through li'an.
التوارث (al-tawāruth): Mutual inheritance between father and child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which two consequences are removed by li'an?
A) Inheritance and maintenance
B) Custody and visitation
C) Guardianship and inheritance
D) All paternal lineage effects

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school limits the effect of li'an on paternity to the removal of inheritance and maintenance only, preserving all other paternal lineage-related rulings.

Explicit Negation of Paternity in Li'an: Abu Yusuf vs. Abu Hanifa
Intra-Hanafi dispute on li'an paternity negation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the requirement of explicit paternity negation in li'an, and apply the relied-upon position to a li'an scenario.

Core Idea
Separation alone does not negate paternity; the qadi must explicitly cut off lineage.

In the li'an process, the qadi pronounces separation between the spouses. But does that automatically negate the child's paternity? The Hanafi school is divided on this point. This passage examines Abu Yusuf's view that explicit wording is required, and why it became the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
What is the exact point of contention? It is whether the qadi's pronouncement of separation (tafriq) alone suffices to negate paternity (nafy al-nasab) or whether an explicit declaration is needed.
2
State the two views
Abu Hanifa holds that separation automatically implies negation. Abu Yusuf (and Muhammad in some transmissions) require the qadi to say explicitly: 'I have cut off the lineage of this child from you' after pronouncing separation.
The author of al-Mabsut declares Abu Yusuf's view the correct one.
3
Analyze the proof for Abu Yusuf's view
Consider the analogy: Even after death, a couple is separated by li'an but paternity is not negated. This shows separation and negation are distinct. Therefore, a separate verbal declaration is necessary for negation.
The passage also discusses related cases from al-Majma' to illustrate the implications.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
If the qadi only says 'I separate you' without explicit negation, under Abu Hanifa the child's lineage is negated; under Abu Yusuf it is not. This affects inheritance, guardianship, and other rights.
The relied-upon position for fatwa is Abu Yusuf's, so in practice the qadi must utter the explicit words.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
When drafting a li'an ruling, ensure the qadi pronounces both: 'I separate you' and 'I cut off the lineage of this child from you.' This is the operative rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي قوله نفي نسبه أي القاضي وألحقه بأمه إشارة إلى أن التفريق بينهما لا يكفي لنفي نسب الولد فلذا روي عن أبي يوسف أنه لا بد أن يقول قطعت نسب هذا الولد عنه بعدما قال فرقت بينكما. وفي المبسوط : هذا هو الصحيح لأنه ليس من ضرورة التفريق نفي النسب كما بعد الموت يفرق بينهما باللعان ولا ينتفي نسبه عنه ؛ كذا في النهاية. وفي المجمع : ولو ماتت بنته المنفية عن ولد فادعاه فنسبه غير ثابت منه أي عند الامام. وقالا : يثبت قيد بموتها لأنها لو كانت حية ثبت نسبها بدعوة ولدها اتفاقاً. وقيد بالبنت لأن الولد المنفي لو كان ذكراً فمات وترك ولداً ثبت نسبه من المدعي وورث الأب منه اتفاقاً لحاجة الولد الثاني إلى ثبوت النسب فبقاؤه كبقاء الأول. وقيد بدعوة الولد لأنه لو ادعى البنت المنفية حية ثبت نسبها اتفاقاً وتمامه في شرحه
And in his saying: 'his negation of lineage' means the qadi, and he attaches him to his mother, indicating that separation between them is not sufficient for negating the child's lineage. Hence it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that he must say: 'I have cut off the lineage of this child from you' after he says 'I have separated you.' And in al-Mabsut: This is the correct view because negation of lineage is not a necessary consequence of separation, just as after death they are separated by li'an but his lineage is not negated from him. Similarly in al-Nihayah. And in al-Majma': If his daughter who is negated from a child dies, and he claims the child, his lineage is not established from him according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa). But the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: it is established, restricted by her death, because if she were alive, her lineage would be established by her child's claim by agreement. And restricted by 'daughter' because if the negated child were male and died leaving a son, his lineage is established from the claimant and the father inherits from him by agreement, due to the second child's need for establishing lineage, so his continued existence is like the existence of the first. And restricted by 'the child's claim' because if he claimed the negated daughter while alive, her lineage is established by agreement, and its completion is in its commentary.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The issue is whether the qadi's pronouncement of separation (tafriq) alone suffices to negate the child's paternity, or whether an explicit statement of cutting off lineage is required. The text reports that Abu Yusuf requires the qadi to say explicitly: 'I have cut off the lineage of this child from you' after saying 'I have separated you.' The author of al-Mabsut deems this the correct view, reasoning that separation does not necessarily imply negation of paternity; for example, if a couple separates by death after li'an, the child's lineage is not negated. The passage then presents a case from al-Majma': if a negated daughter dies leaving a child, and her father (the husband who denied her) claims that child, Abu Hanifa holds that the child's lineage to the grandfather is not established, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that it is established, because the child's need for lineage is analogous to the original child's existence. The text also notes that the dispute is restricted by conditions: it applies to a daughter, not a son (because a son's child would establish lineage by agreement), and it applies when the daughter is dead (because if alive, the child's claim would establish lineage by consensus).

Key Terms
التفريق (al-tafrīq): The qadi's pronouncement of separation between the spouses as a result of li'an.
نفي النسب (nafy al-nasab): Judicial declaration that the child is not the legal offspring of the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 'This child is not yours'
B) 'I have cut off the lineage of this child from you'
C) 'You are divorced'
D) Nothing; separation suffices

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position requires the qadi to explicitly state the negation of paternity in li'an; separation alone does not suffice.

Li'an for Impotent Men: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the contradictory rulings on li'an for impotent men and reconcile them by identifying the condition of emission.

Core Idea
Li'an for impotent men depends on the ability to emit fluid—if possible, paternity can be established and li'an is prescribed.

In this passage, the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding whether li'an (mutual imprecation) is prescribed for a man who is physically incapable of normal intercourse (majbub or khasi). The source al-Dhakhira states it is not, but a critical comment from al-Fath objects that if the man can emit fluid through rubbing, paternity is possible and li'an applies. The author reconciles the views by conditioning the ruling on emission. Let's unpack the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opposing positions
State the view from al-Dhakhira that li'an is not prescribed for the majbub and khasi, and the objection from al-Fath that li'an should be prescribed because emission is possible.
The passage cites al-Dhakhira's absolute denial, then al-Fath's critique.
2
Analyze the basis of each position
Al-Dhakhira's basis: a child cannot be attributed to such a man because normal intercourse is impossible. Al-Fath's basis: the majbub can emit fluid through rubbing (sahq), so paternity is legally possible.
Emission is the key factual element.
3
Reconcile the views
The author notes that al-Dhakhira's ruling is conditional on no emission; if the man does not emit, li'an is not prescribed. If he does emit, the mukhtar (chosen) view applies and li'an is prescribed.
The reconciliation preserves both texts by adding a condition.
4
Connect to broader Hanafi principles
The same condition appears in the chapter on 'iddah, where the khasi is treated like a healthy man regarding paternity and 'iddah if he emits, otherwise like a minor.
This shows consistency across the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الذخيرة : لا يشرع اللعان بنفي لا الولد في المجبوب والخصي ومن يولد له ولد. قوله: (وفي الذخيرة لا يشرع اللعان بنفي الولد في الخصي والمجبوب الخ) لأنه لا يلحق به الولد ؛ كذا في الفتح عن الذخيرة. ثم قال : وفيه نظر لأن المجبوب ينزل بالسحق ويثبت نسب ولده على ما هو المختار اهـ. أي فما هنا على خلاف المختار أو هو مبني على ما إذا كان لا ينزل، وسيذكر المؤلف في العدة عن كافي الحاكم والخصي كالصحيح في الولد والعدة وكذا المجبوب إذا كان ينزل وإلا لم يلزمه الولد فكان بمنزلة الصبي في الولد والعدة .اهـ. ويأتي قريباً في أول باب العنين ما يؤيده .
And in al-Dhakhira: Li'an is not prescribed for negating the child in the case of the impotent man (majbub), the castrated man (khasi), and one from whom a child is born. His statement: '(And in al-Dhakhira: li'an is not prescribed for negating the child in the castrated and impotent man, etc.) because the child cannot be attributed to him; as in al-Fath from al-Dhakhira. Then he said: But there is a flaw because the majbub can emit fluid through rubbing, and his child's lineage is established according to the chosen view. So what is here is contrary to the chosen view, or it is based on the case when he does not emit. And the author will mention in the chapter on 'iddah from Kafi al-Hakim that the khasi is like a healthy man regarding the child and the 'iddah, and likewise the majbub if he emits; otherwise the child is not attributed to him, and he is like a boy regarding the child and the 'iddah. And soon in the beginning of the chapter on the impotent (al-'innin) what supports this will come.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether li'an is prescribed for men who are physically incapable of procreation (majbub: one whose penis is cut off; khasi: one whose testicles are removed). Al-Dhakhira states that li'an is not prescribed for them because a child cannot legally be attributed to them. However, the commentator from al-Fath raises an objection: a majbub can still emit fluid through rubbing (sahq), and therefore if a child is conceived from that emission, paternity can be established. The author reconciles the two positions by noting that the ruling in al-Dhakhira is based on the case where the man does not emit, while if he does emit, he is like a normal man and li'an is prescribed. The author also references a later passage in the chapter on 'iddah where the khasi is treated like a healthy man regarding paternity and waiting period, and the majbub is treated similarly if he emits. This shows that the rule is conditional on the ability to father a child.

Key Terms
المجبوب (al-majbūb): A man whose penis has been amputated or damaged so that he cannot have normal intercourse, but may still emit fluid.
الخصي (al-khaṣī): A castrated man whose testicles are removed.
السحق (al-saḥq): Rubbing or friction that can cause emission of semen.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) If he can emit fluid through rubbing
C) Never
D) Only if he admits the child

Key Takeaway
Li'an for impotent men is allowed if they can emit fluid, as paternity is then possible; otherwise it is not.

Effect of Retracting Accusation (Ikdhab) After Li'an
Explains the hadd and paternity consequences of the husband's retraction after li'an.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that retraction after li'an subjects the husband to hadd and identify the underlying qiyas with witnesses of zina.

Core Idea
Retraction after li'an triggers hadd due to the implicit accusation in li'an itself, not the original qadhf.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the consequences when a husband who performed li'an later retracts his accusation. It clarifies that the hadd punishment is based on the accusation implicit in the li'an, analogous to retracting witnesses. Several nuanced scenarios and an intra-Hanafi disagreement are also presented.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on retraction after li'an
The passage states that retraction after li'an subjects the husband to hadd (flogging) for qadhf. Note the hukm level: wajib.
This is the core ruling.
2
Understand the basis of the hadd
The hadd is not based on the original qadhf accusation because the husband already fulfilled its consequence by li'an. Rather, it is based on the implicit accusation contained in the words of li'an itself.
This is a key point: the retraction reveals that the li'an accusation was false.
3
Examine the qiyas (analogy) to witnesses
The text analogizes the husband's retraction to witnesses of zina who retract their testimony; in both cases, they are flogged because their words implied an accusation of zina.
This is a jaliyyah qiyas.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on paternity
If the husband retracts after li'an and the child left a daughter who has a son, Imam Muhammad holds that the child's lineage is established from the husband, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf disagree.
This affects inheritance and other rulings.
5
Distinguish before/after li'an and other scenarios
If the husband retracts before li'an and has not divorced, he is flogged. But if he has given an irrevocable divorce, no hadd and no li'an. The order of words in the accusation also matters.
These nuanced cases show the school's detailed understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القذف. ويحد، الولوالجية. وشمل الإكذاب صريحاً وضمناً ولهذا لو مات الولد المنفي عن مال فادعى الملاعن لا يثبت نسبه ويحد، فإن كان قد ترك ولداً ثبت نسبه من الأب وورثه الأب لاحتياج الحي إلى النسب، ولو ترك بنتاً ولها ابن فأكذب الملاعن نفسه يثبت نسب الولد منه عند الإمام خلافاً لهما؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وظاهر ما في الكتاب أن الإكذاب بعد اللعان ووجوب الحد عليه ليس باعتبار قذفه الأول لأنه أخذ بموجبه وهو اللعان بل باعتبار القذف الثاني الذي تضمنه كلمات اللعان كشهود الزنا إذا رجعوا فإنهم يحدون باعتبار ما تضمنته شهادتهم من أما إذا أكذب نفسه قبل اللعان ينظر؛ فإن لم يطلقها قبل الإكذاب حد أيضاً، وإن أبانها ثم أكذب نفسه فلا حد ولا لعان لأن اللعان أثره التفريق بينهما وهو لا يتأتى بعد البينونة لحصوله بالإبانة وهو لا يصح بدون حكمه ولا يجب الحد لأن قذفه وقع موجباً للعان فلا ينقلب موجباً للحد. وعلى هذا لو قال يا زانية أنت طالق ثلاثاً لا حد ولا لعان، ولو قال أنت طالق ثلاثاً يا زانية حد أطلق في الإكذاب فشمل ما إذا أنكر الولد بعدما ادعاه ولذا قال أيضاً في فتح القدير : لو أقامت البينة على الزوج أنه ادعاه وهو ينكر يثبت النسب منه ويحد وفي جامع الصدر :الشهيد قذفها بنفي الولد ولا عن فتزوجت غيره فادعاه فإن ولدت من الثاني فنفاه لاعن وينتفي إن علق بعد إكذابه وقبله لا، وينبغي أن لا يلاعن لاستناده نظیره زنيت وأنت صبية بخلاف وأنت ذمية أو رقيق أو منذ أربعين سنة ) عشرون سنة وإن تردد يقطع استحساناً وقياساً لا نظيره أسلمت زوجته أو أعتقت ثم ولدت فنفاه ا هـ. ثم اعلم أن ولد أم الولد إذا نفاه المولى وقلنا بصحته فإن حكمه حكم ولد المنكوحة إذا نفي في سائر الأحكام فلا تقبل شهادة أحد للآخر بعد إعتاق الولد، ولا يضع أحدهما زكاته فيه، وتحرم المناكحة بينهما، ولا يرث أحدهما صاحبه بالقرابة لكن المولى يرث منه بالولاء إذا لم يكن عصبة أقرب منه، وتجب نفقته على المولى بعد إعتاقه بحكم الملك؛ كذا في شرح التلخيص من الشهادات
Al-qadhf. And he is flogged. al-Walawaljiyyah [unclear]. And it includes retraction (ikdhab) explicitly and implicitly. Hence, if the negated child dies leaving property, and the one who performed li'an claims it, his lineage is not established and he is flogged. But if he left a son, his lineage is established from the father and the father inherits from him because the living child needs lineage. And if he left a daughter who has a son, and the one who performed li'an retracts, the child's lineage is established from him according to Imam Muhammad, contrary to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And the apparent meaning of what is in the book is that retraction after li'an and the obligation of hadd upon him is not based on his first accusation, because he fulfilled its consequence which is li'an, but rather based on the second accusation that is contained in the words of li'an, like witnesses of zina when they retract: they are flogged based on what their testimony contained. As for if he retracts before li'an, it is considered: if he did not divorce her before the retraction, he is also flogged. But if he gave her an irrevocable divorce (bā'in) then retracted, there is no hadd and no li'an, because the effect of li'an is separation, which is not possible after irrevocable divorce, and it is not valid without its ruling, and hadd is not obligatory because his accusation was subject to li'an and so cannot become subject to hadd. Hence, if he says 'O fornicator, you are thrice divorced,' there is no hadd and no li'an. But if he says 'You are thrice divorced, O fornicator,' he is flogged. He made retraction general, so it includes when he denies the child after claiming it. Hence, it is also said in Fath al-Qadir: If she brings evidence that the husband claimed the child and then denies it, the lineage is established from him and he is flogged. And in Jami' al-Sadr al-Shahid: He accused her by negating the child and performed li'an, then she married another and he claimed the child. If she gives birth from the second, he negates it and performs li'an, and it is negated if it is after his retraction; before it, not. And he should not perform li'an because it is based on his like 'fornicated' and you were a minor, contrary to 'and you were a dhimmi' or 'a slave' or 'forty years ago'—twenty years even if doubtful, it is cut off by istihsan and not by qiyas. Like: his wife converted or was freed then gave birth and he negated it. Then know that the child of an umm walad, if the master negates him and we hold it valid, its ruling is like the ruling of the child of a lawful wife when negated in all other rulings: so one's testimony for the other is not accepted after the child is freed, and neither places his zakat on the other, and marriage between them is forbidden, and neither inherits from the other by kinship, but the master inherits from him by wala' if there is no nearer agnate, and his maintenance is obligatory upon the master after freeing him by virtue of ownership. Thus in Sharh al-Talkhis from the chapter on testimonies.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, using analogy, and covers the effects of the husband retracting (ikdhab) his accusation after performing li'an. The text begins by stating that retraction subjects the husband to hadd (flogging for qadhf). It explains that the hadd is not based on the original accusation but on the implicit accusation contained in the li'an itself, analogous to witnesses of zina who, when they retract, are flogged for the accusation implied in their testimony. The passage then distinguishes various scenarios: if the child dies leaving property and the husband claims it, he is flogged and the child's lineage is not established; but if the child leaves a son, the husband inherits because the living child's need for lineage prevails. There is also a dispute between Imam Muhammad (who holds that if the husband retracts and the child left a daughter who has a son, the lineage is established) and Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (who disagree). The text also discusses retraction before li'an: if the husband retracts before li'an and has not divorced her, he is flogged; but if he has already given an irrevocable divorce (bā'in), then no hadd and no li'an because the purpose of li'an (separation) is already achieved. Additional cases include varying the order of words ('O fornicator, you are thrice divorced' vs. 'You are thrice divorced, O fornicator') and the effect on paternity negation. Finally, the passage notes that the ruling for the child of an umm walad (slave mother) when the master negates him is analogous to the child of a free wife: no inheritance between them, prohibition of marriage, and the master inherits by wala'.

Key Terms
الإكذاب (al-ikdhāb): The husband's retraction of his accusation of zina after performing li'an.
الحد (al-ḥadd): The fixed punishment for qadhf (false accusation of zina), which is 80 lashes.
القذف (al-qadhf): Accusing a married person of zina without four witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the husband retracts his accusation after li'an, what is his punishment according to the passage?
A) No punishment
B) He is flogged for qadhf
C) He must perform li'an again
D) He loses custody of the child

Key Takeaway
Retraction after li'an subjects the husband to hadd for qadhf due to the implicit accusation in li'an, with nuanced effects on paternity depending on surviving heirs.

Remarriage After Li'an Retraction: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on remarriage after retraction in li'an, with internal Hanafi disagreement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on remarriage after li'an retraction and distinguish Abu Yusuf's dissenting view.

Core Idea
Li'an separation is temporary; retraction permits remarriage — except according to Abu Yusuf, who deems it permanent.

Li'an creates a separation that prohibits cohabitation and marriage as long as both parties maintain their positions. But what happens if one retracts? The majority of Hanafi imams allow remarriage, but Abu Yusuf holds it becomes permanently forbidden. This lesson unpacks the dispute and identifies the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act under discussion? The husband's remarriage of his wife after li'an separation. The matn states 'wa lahu an yankihaha' — he may marry her. But this is qualified by retraction.
The text clarifies that the permissibility applies when either party retracts.
2
State the majority Hanafi view
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the prohibition is temporary. Retraction removes it entirely, allowing remarriage and cohabitation.
This is also the view of the matn and the commentator.
3
Identify the dissenting voice
Abu Yusuf (the 'second') holds that li'an creates a permanent prohibition (ḥurmat mu’abbadah) akin to the prohibition of fosterage (ridaʿ).
This would mean the couple can never remarry, even after retraction.
4
Compare the proofs
The majority rely on the general nature of retraction removing the cause of prohibition. Abu Yusuf analogizes li'an to other permanent prohibitions. The text does not provide detailed proofs but states the positions.
The commentator notes that the restriction of permissibility to flogging is not a point of dispute.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: retraction allows remarriage. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
The text uses the phrase 'فالحاصل' to summarize the conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وله أن ينكحها أي للملاعن بعد التفريق أن يتزوجها إذا أكذب نفسه . أطلقه فشمل ما إذا حد أو لم يحد فتقييد الشارح الحل بالحد اتفاقي، وكذا إذا أكذبت نفسها فصدقته. فالحاصل أن الفرقة باللعان يزول بها ملك النكاح وتوجب حرمة الاجتماع والتزوج ما داما على حال اللعان فإن أكذب أحدهما نفسه جاز التناكح والاجتماع عند الإمام والثالث. وقال الثاني : إنها توجب حرمة مؤبدة كحرمة الرضاع
His statement: 'And he may marry her' means that the one who performed li'an, after separation, may marry her if he retracts himself. He made it general, so it includes whether he was flogged or not, so the commentator's restriction of permissibility to flogging is by agreement. Likewise if she retracts herself and he confirms her. The conclusion is that separation by li'an removes the marital bond and necessitates prohibition of cohabitation and marriage as long as they remain in the state of li'an. If one of them retracts, marriage and cohabitation become permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa and the third (Muhammad). And the second (Abu Yusuf) said: It necessitates a permanent prohibition like the prohibition of fosterage.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of li'an on the possibility of remarriage. The text comments on the statement 'and he may marry her' from the matn. The author explains that the husband may remarry his wife after li'an if he retracts his accusation (ikdhab). This ruling applies whether or not he was flogged. Similarly, if the wife retracts and the husband confirms her, remarriage is permissible. The general principle is that li'an only prohibits cohabitation and marriage during the state of li'an; if either party retracts, the prohibition is lifted. This is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the 'third'). However, Abu Yusuf (the 'second') holds that li'an creates a permanent prohibition like that of fosterage (rida'), meaning the couple can never remarry. The commentary notes that the commentator's restriction of permissibility to the case of flogging is by agreement (i.e., not a point of dispute). The relied-upon view is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Key Terms
الفرقة باللعان (al-furqah bi al-li‘ān): The separation between spouses that results from the process of li'an.
حرمة الاجتماع (ḥurmat al-ijtimā‘): The prohibition of the spouses being together as husband and wife.
حرمة مؤبدة (ḥurmat mu’abbadah): A permanent prohibition that lasts forever.

Key Takeaway
