تكون حرة لأن زوج الأمة إذا كان محبوباً أو عنيناً فالخيار إلى أقول : إن هذا حاله دون حال العنين لإمكان زوال عنته فيصل إليها وهو مستحيل هنا فحكمه حكم المجبوب بجامع أنه لا يمكنه إدخال آلته القصيرة داخل الفرج فالضرر الحاصل للمرأة به مساو لضرر المجبوب فلها طلب التفريق وبهذا ظهر أن انتفاء التفريق لا وجه له وهو من القنية فلا يسلم ا هـ. وقد علمت نقله هنا عن المحيط أيضاً فعدم تسليمه ممنوع قوله : ( وبعد التأجيل في العنين لأن الجنون الخ) قال في البدائع : وإن كان الزوج كبيراً مجنوناً فوجدته عنيناً قالوا: إنه لا يؤجل؛ كذا ذكر الكرخي لأن التأجيل للتفريق عند عدم الدخول وفرقة العنين طلاق والمجنون لا يملك الطلاق. وذكر القاضي في شرح مختصر الطحاوي أنه ينتظر حولاً ولا ينتظر إلى إفاقته بخلاف الصبي لأن الصغر مانع من الوصول فيتأني إلى أن يزول الصغر ثم يؤجل سنة . فأما الجنون فلا يمنع الوصول لأن المجنون يجامع فيولج للحال. والصحيح ما ذكره الكرخي أنه لا يؤجل أصلاً لما ذكرنا ا هـ. ومقتضى هذا لا يؤجل، ولا يفرق إذا كان المجنون مجبوباً إذ لا فرق بين المجبوب والعنين في العلة
Book of Divorce, Chapter on the Impotent and Others. Among women, the source of 'inna. Some explicitly stated that one should not say 'aneen due to 'anna as the jurists say, for it is fallen speech. He said: The well-known in this meaning as Tha'lab and others said is a man 'aneen between al-ta'neen and al-'unna. And in al-Bari' it is al-'anana with fatha. Al-Azhari said: He is called 'aneen because his penis turns (ya'unn) at the woman's vulva to right and left, turning aside when he wants to insert. Thus in al-Misbah. Its plural is 'unun. As for the jurists, he is one who cannot reach [intercourse] despite having an erect organ due to a disease, even if he can reach a previously married woman but not a virgin, or some women but not others, whether his organ becomes erect or not, as in al-'Inaya. Hence it was said in Sharh al-Manzooma: al-shakkaz (with a fatha on the mu'jama, shadda on the kaf, and after alif a zay) is one who, when he draws the woman, ejaculates before intermixing, then his organ does not become erect thereafter for intercourse. He is of the category of 'aneen; she has the right to demand separation. And even if he can reach a previously married woman but not a virgin, or some women but not others, due to weakness of nature or old age or sorcery, he is 'aneen in the right of whom he cannot reach, because the purpose is lost for her. For sorcery in our view is real in existence and conception, and its effect is real as in al-Muhit. He is not removed from 'inna by inserting in her anus, contrary to Ibn 'Aqil, for he says the anus is more severe than the vulva. Thus in al-Mi'raj. And in it: If he only inserted the glans, he is not 'aneen. And if he is mutilated (maqtu'ha), then insertion of the rest of the penis is necessary. It should be said that insertion to the extent of the glans from the mutilated part suffices. And I have not seen the ruling if his penis is cut off, and the absolute term 'majbub' includes it, and it is in Tahrir al-Shafi'iyya, but their statement 'if she is satisfied with it then no option for her' contradicts it. And it has two parallels: one, if the tenant destroyed the house; second, if the seller destroyed the commodity before delivery. His saying: (She found her husband majbub, separation is immediate) — he is one whose penis and testicles are removed; it is said jababtuhu jabban from the chapter qatala 'I cut him off,' and he is majbub between al-jubab with fatha and kasr. Thus in al-Misbah. And no delay is given because there is no benefit. And since the separation is for loss of her right, it depends on her demand; he did not mention it here, contenting with what he mentioned in the 'aneen. And he indicated that if it became necessary after having reached her once, she has no option, as if he becomes 'aneen thereafter. And attached to the majbub is one whose penis is very small, like a button; not one whose penis cannot be inserted into the vagina at all — then she has no right to demand separation. Thus in al-Muhit. Its apparent meaning is that if it cannot be inserted at all, he is like the majbub due to his restriction to 'inside'; and he made the husband 'majbub' absolute, so it includes the small and the sick, unlike the 'aneen where one waits for his attainment of puberty or cure due to possibility of removal. And he intended: his organ was short, which necessarily implies her consent. There is contemplation in it, for although it is not necessary rationally, it is necessary customarily, as if she married him knowing his condition, and intercourse is her right, and she has lost her vulva. His saying: (One of them: if the tenant destroyed the house). Al-Ramli said: meaning he cannot rescind the lease due to this defect because he is the one who caused it. And his saying: (if the seller destroyed the commodity) means he cannot demand the price because he himself invalidated his right by destroying the commodity. His saying: (one whose penis is very small like a button) with kasr of the zay, plural azrar. His saying: (not one whose organ is short, etc.) al-Shurnbulali discussed it in his commentary on al-Wahbaniyya and said: A woman who has the right to demand intercourse, because if she is a minor, her puberty is awaited in the case of majbub and 'aneen for possibility of her consent, unlike if one of them is insane, then one does not wait for his sanity in castration and 'inna due to lack of benefit, and separation is immediate in castration, and after a delay in 'inna because insanity does not eliminate desire; with the guardianship of a guardian if there is one, otherwise one appointed by the judge. And if the guardian brings evidence in the two cases of her satisfaction with his 'inna or jabb, or of her knowledge of his condition at the time of contract, no separation is made. And if her oath is demanded on that, she swears; if she refuses, no separation; if she swears, separation is made. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And they said: If the wife of a majbub brings a child after separation within two years, his lineage is established and the separation is not invalidated, unlike the 'aneen where the separation is invalidated because when his lineage is established, he is no longer 'aneen. The commentator objected that the divorce occurred by his separation, and it is irrevocable, so how can it be invalidated? Do you not see that if she confessed after separation that he had reached her, the separation is not invalidated. The answer is that establishment of lineage from the majbub is due to ejaculation by [؟] friction, and the separation between them is due to castration, which is present. Unlike its establishment from the 'aneen, for it shows he is not 'aneen, and the separation was based on that. Unlike what he adduced from her confession, for she is suspect in invalidating the judgment due to possibility of falsehood. So it appeared that the research was far-fetched, as in Fath al-Qadir. In al-Khaniyya from the section on 'aneen: If two witnesses testify after the judge's separation to the wife's confession before separation that he reached her, the judge's separation is invalidated. And if she confessed after separation that he had reached her, she is not believed to invalidate the judge's separation. End. The conclusion is that the judge's separation in 'aneen is invalidated by the coming of a child and by establishing evidence of her confession of reaching. And in al-Tatar Khaniyya: If the husband was majbub and she did not know his condition, then she brought a child and he claimed it and the judge established his lineage, then she learned his condition and demanded separation, she has that right. End. And he made it absolute regarding the woman, and it must be restricted that she is not a raqba (with a closed vagina), for if a raqba finds him majbub, she has no option, as in al-Khaniyya; and that she be free, for the wife of a slave if he is majbub or 'aneen, the option belongs to... I say: This condition is unlike that of 'aneen because removal of his 'inna is possible so he may reach her, yet here it is impossible, so his ruling is the ruling of the majbub due to the common factor that he cannot insert his short organ inside the vagina, so the harm to the woman is equal to the harm of the majbub. Thus she has the right to demand separation, and by this it is clear that denial of separation has no basis, and it is from al-Qunniya so it is not accepted. End. It has been known that his transmission here from al-Muhit also, so its non-acceptance is objectionable. His saying: (And after the delay in 'aneen because insanity, etc.) He said in al-Bada'i': If the husband is an adult insane and she found him 'aneen, they said: he is not given a delay; thus al-Karkhi mentioned because the delay is for separation at the time of non-entry, and the separation of the 'aneen is talaq, and the insane does not own talaq. And al-Qadhi mentioned in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi that one waits a year and does not wait for his sanity, unlike the minor because minority prevents reaching, so one waits until minority ends, then gives a year. As for insanity, it does not prevent reaching because the insane copulates, so he inserts immediately. And the correct is what al-Karkhi mentioned that he is not given a delay at all for what we mentioned. End. And this requires that delay is not given, and no separation is made if the insane is majbub, for there is no difference between majbub and 'aneen in the cause.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addressing the chapter on impotence (al-'inna) and related conditions within the Book of Divorce. The author begins by providing the philological and juristic definitions of the 'aneen (impotent man) and then discusses the majbub (castrated man). The key legal ruling is that a wife who discovers her husband is majbub may demand immediate separation without any waiting period, because there is no hope of cure. In contrast, an 'aneen is given a one-year deferment (taraddud) to allow for possible recovery. The text also makes several important distinctions: a man who can penetrate some women but not others is still considered 'aneen with respect to the woman he cannot penetrate; a man with a very small penis (like a button) is likened to a majbub; and a man who cannot insert at all is treated as majbub. The commentary then examines the case of an insane 'aneen: according to al-Karkhi, no deferment is given because the insane cannot pronounce talaq and the separation is a form of talaq. However, al-Qadhi held that a year's deferment is given (but not until sanity). The relied-upon position is that of al-Karkhi. Additionally, the text discusses the effect of a child born after separation: for a majbub, the child's lineage is established but does not invalidate the separation; for an 'aneen, the birth of a child invalidates the separation because it proves he is not impotent. The wife who was unaware of her husband's condition at the time of marriage has the right to seek separation, but if she knowingly married him, she is deemed to have consented. Special conditions apply: the wife must be free and not have a closed vagina (ratqa'), as such women are considered satisfied by any penetration. The passage ends with a marginal note analogizing a man with a very short penis to a majbub due to the harm caused.

Key Terms
العنين (al-'aneen): Linguistically: a man whose penis turns away at the vagina. Juristically: a man who cannot penetrate due to a disease, even if he can penetrate some women but not others, or has an erect organ.
المجبوب (al-majbub): A man whose penis and testicles have been removed (castrated). The ruling is that his wife may demand immediate separation without delay.
الشكاز (al-shakkaz): A man who ejaculates before intercourse and then his penis does not become erect again. He is considered like an 'aneen in that the wife can demand separation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling regarding a wife who discovers her husband is majbub (castrated)?
A) She must wait one year to see if he recovers.
B) She can demand immediate separation without any waiting period.
C) She cannot demand separation under any circumstances.
D) She must wait until her husband's sanity returns.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between the 'aneen, who is given a one-year deferment for possible recovery, and the majbub, for whom separation is immediate due to incurability.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Insane 'Aneen and Analogous Cases
Intra-Hanafi dispute and qiyas on extended cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute between al-Karkhi and al-Qadhi regarding the insane 'aneen, and apply the analogy (qiyas) for a man with a very short organ to the ruling of the majbub.

Core Idea
An insane 'aneen gets no deferment—because he cannot pronounce talaq; a man with a button-sized organ is like a majbub—immediate separation for incurable harm.

This lesson dives into the nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about the insane 'aneen: should he be given a one-year deferment? Al-Karkhi says no, because the separation is a talaq that the insane cannot effect; al-Qadhi says yes, because intercourse is possible despite insanity. The text settles on al-Karkhi's view. We also examine the qiyas (analogy) that extends the ruling of the majbub to a man with an extremely short organ, based on the common illa of inability to achieve penetration with no hope of cure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
The dispute is about whether an insane 'aneen husband gets a one-year deferment before the wife can seek separation.
The insane cannot pronounce talaq.
2
State al-Karkhi's position and proof
Al-Karkhi: No deferment because the separation is talaq and the insane cannot execute talaq.
The deferment becomes pointless if the husband cannot effect the divorce.
3
State al-Qadhi's position and proof
Al-Qadhi: Deferment of one year, not waiting for sanity, because insanity does not prevent intercourse.
Analogous to a minor who gets deferment until puberty.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response and tarjih
The author (Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) sides with al-Karkhi, as the minor's inability is due to minority, not similar to insanity.
Also, the insane cannot issue talaq even if he recovers.
5
Apply the qiyas for the short organ
A man whose penis is so short it cannot enter the vagina is analogous to a majbub. The common illa is impossibility of penetration with no hope of cure.
This is based on tahqiq al-manat (verification of the effective cause).

Book of Divorce, Chapter on the Impotent and Others. Among women, the source of 'inna. Some explicitly stated that one should not say 'aneen due to 'anna as the jurists say, for it is fallen speech. He said: The well-known in this meaning as Tha'lab and others said is a man 'aneen between al-ta'neen and al-'unna. And in al-Bari' it is al-'anana with fatha. Al-Azhari said: He is called 'aneen because his penis turns (ya'unn) at the woman's vulva to right and left, turning aside when he wants to insert. Thus in al-Misbah. Its plural is 'unun. As for the jurists, he is one who cannot reach [intercourse] despite having an erect organ due to a disease, even if he can reach a previously married woman but not a virgin, or some women but not others, whether his organ becomes erect or not, as in al-'Inaya. Hence it was said in Sharh al-Manzooma: al-shakkaz (with a fatha on the mu'jama, shadda on the kaf, and after alif a zay) is one who, when he draws the woman, ejaculates before intermixing, then his organ does not become erect thereafter for intercourse. He is of the category of 'aneen; she has the right to demand separation. And even if he can reach a previously married woman but not a virgin, or some women but not others, due to weakness of nature or old age or sorcery, he is 'aneen in the right of whom he cannot reach, because the purpose is lost for her. For sorcery in our view is real in existence and conception, and its effect is real as in al-Muhit. He is not removed from 'inna by inserting in her anus, contrary to Ibn 'Aqil, for he says the anus is more severe than the vulva. Thus in al-Mi'raj. And in it: If he only inserted the glans, he is not 'aneen. And if he is mutilated (maqtu'ha), then insertion of the rest of the penis is necessary. It should be said that insertion to the extent of the glans from the mutilated part suffices. And I have not seen the ruling if his penis is cut off, and the absolute term 'majbub' includes it, and it is in Tahrir al-Shafi'iyya, but their statement 'if she is satisfied with it then no option for her' contradicts it. And it has two parallels: one, if the tenant destroyed the house; second, if the seller destroyed the commodity before delivery. His saying: (She found her husband majbub, separation is immediate) — he is one whose penis and testicles are removed; it is said jababtuhu jabban from the chapter qatala 'I cut him off,' and he is majbub between al-jubab with fatha and kasr. Thus in al-Misbah. And no delay is given because there is no benefit. And since the separation is for loss of her right, it depends on her demand; he did not mention it here, contenting with what he mentioned in the 'aneen. And he indicated that if it became necessary after having reached her once, she has no option, as if he becomes 'aneen thereafter. And attached to the majbub is one whose penis is very small, like a button; not one whose penis cannot be inserted into the vagina at all — then she has no right to demand separation. Thus in al-Muhit. Its apparent meaning is that if it cannot be inserted at all, he is like the majbub due to his restriction to 'inside'; and he made the husband 'majbub' absolute, so it includes the small and the sick, unlike the 'aneen where one waits for his attainment of puberty or cure due to possibility of removal. And he intended: his organ was short, which necessarily implies her consent. There is contemplation in it, for although it is not necessary rationally, it is necessary customarily, as if she married him knowing his condition, and intercourse is her right, and she has lost her vulva. His saying: (One of them: if the tenant destroyed the house). Al-Ramli said: meaning he cannot rescind the lease due to this defect because he is the one who caused it. And his saying: (if the seller destroyed the commodity) means he cannot demand the price because he himself invalidated his right by destroying the commodity. His saying: (one whose penis is very small like a button) with kasr of the zay, plural azrar. His saying: (not one whose organ is short, etc.) al-Shurnbulali discussed it in his commentary on al-Wahbaniyya and said: A woman who has the right to demand intercourse, because if she is a minor, her puberty is awaited in the case of majbub and 'aneen for possibility of her consent, unlike if one of them is insane, then one does not wait for his sanity in castration and 'inna due to lack of benefit, and separation is immediate in castration, and after a delay in 'inna because insanity does not eliminate desire; with the guardianship of a guardian if there is one, otherwise one appointed by the judge. And if the guardian brings evidence in the two cases of her satisfaction with his 'inna or jabb, or of her knowledge of his condition at the time of contract, no separation is made. And if her oath is demanded on that, she swears; if she refuses, no separation; if she swears, separation is made. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And they said: If the wife of a majbub brings a child after separation within two years, his lineage is established and the separation is not invalidated, unlike the 'aneen where the separation is invalidated because when his lineage is established, he is no longer 'aneen. The commentator objected that the divorce occurred by his separation, and it is irrevocable, so how can it be invalidated? Do you not see that if she confessed after separation that he had reached her, the separation is not invalidated. The answer is that establishment of lineage from the majbub is due to ejaculation by [؟] friction, and the separation between them is due to castration, which is present. Unlike its establishment from the 'aneen, for it shows he is not 'aneen, and the separation was based on that. Unlike what he adduced from her confession, for she is suspect in invalidating the judgment due to possibility of falsehood. So it appeared that the research was far-fetched, as in Fath al-Qadir. In al-Khaniyya from the section on 'aneen: If two witnesses testify after the judge's separation to the wife's confession before separation that he reached her, the judge's separation is invalidated. And if she confessed after separation that he had reached her, she is not believed to invalidate the judge's separation. End. The conclusion is that the judge's separation in 'aneen is invalidated by the coming of a child and by establishing evidence of her confession of reaching. And in al-Tatar Khaniyya: If the husband was majbub and she did not know his condition, then she brought a child and he claimed it and the judge established his lineage, then she learned his condition and demanded separation, she has that right. End. And he made it absolute regarding the woman, and it must be restricted that she is not a raqba (with a closed vagina), for if a raqba finds him majbub, she has no option, as in al-Khaniyya; and that she be free, for the wife of a slave if he is majbub or 'aneen, the option belongs to... I say: This condition is unlike that of 'aneen because removal of his 'inna is possible so he may reach her, yet here it is impossible, so his ruling is the ruling of the majbub due to the common factor that he cannot insert his short organ inside the vagina, so the harm to the woman is equal to the harm of the majbub. Thus she has the right to demand separation, and by this it is clear that denial of separation has no basis, and it is from al-Qunniya so it is not accepted. End. It has been known that his transmission here from al-Muhit also, so its non-acceptance is objectionable. His saying: (And after the delay in 'aneen because insanity, etc.) He said in al-Bada'i': If the husband is an adult insane and she found him 'aneen, they said: he is not given a delay; thus al-Karkhi mentioned because the delay is for separation at the time of non-entry, and the separation of the 'aneen is talaq, and the insane does not own talaq. And al-Qadhi mentioned in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi that one waits a year and does not wait for his sanity, unlike the minor because minority prevents reaching, so one waits until minority ends, then gives a year. As for insanity, it does not prevent reaching because the insane copulates, so he inserts immediately. And the correct is what al-Karkhi mentioned that he is not given a delay at all for what we mentioned. End. And this requires that delay is not given, and no separation is made if the insane is majbub, for there is no difference between majbub and 'aneen in the cause.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addressing the chapter on impotence (al-'inna) and related conditions within the Book of Divorce. The author begins by providing the philological and juristic definitions of the 'aneen (impotent man) and then discusses the majbub (castrated man). The key legal ruling is that a wife who discovers her husband is majbub may demand immediate separation without any waiting period, because there is no hope of cure. In contrast, an 'aneen is given a one-year deferment (taraddud) to allow for possible recovery. The text also makes several important distinctions: a man who can penetrate some women but not others is still considered 'aneen with respect to the woman he cannot penetrate; a man with a very small penis (like a button) is likened to a majbub; and a man who cannot insert at all is treated as majbub. The commentary then examines the case of an insane 'aneen: according to al-Karkhi, no deferment is given because the insane cannot pronounce talaq and the separation is a form of talaq. However, al-Qadhi held that a year's deferment is given (but not until sanity). The relied-upon position is that of al-Karkhi. Additionally, the text discusses the effect of a child born after separation: for a majbub, the child's lineage is established but does not invalidate the separation; for an 'aneen, the birth of a child invalidates the separation because it proves he is not impotent. The wife who was unaware of her husband's condition at the time of marriage has the right to seek separation, but if she knowingly married him, she is deemed to have consented. Special conditions apply: the wife must be free and not have a closed vagina (ratqa'), as such women are considered satisfied by any penetration. The passage ends with a marginal note analogizing a man with a very short penis to a majbub due to the harm caused.

Key Terms
العنين (al-'aneen): A man who cannot penetrate due to a disease, even if partially.
المجبوب (al-majbub): Castrated man with removal of penis and testicles.
الزر (al-zirr (button)): A metaphor for a very short penis that cannot penetrate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling for an insane 'aneen husband?
A) She must wait one year for possible recovery.
B) She may demand immediate separation because no deferment is given.
C) She must wait until her husband regains sanity.
D) She cannot seek separation because the condition is not his fault.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on the insane 'aneen is resolved by al-Karkhi's view that no deferment is given, because the separation is a talaq and the insane cannot issue it.

The Hanafi Ruling on Separation for Eunuch and Impotent
Ruling with proof on judicial separation for eunuch and impotent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when a wife can seek separation from a eunuch versus an impotent man, and apply the conditions for immediate or delayed separation.

Core Idea
A eunuch is separated immediately due to permanent defect; an impotent man is given a one-year delay.

This lesson examines the Hanafi distinction between a eunuch (majbub) and an impotent man ('anin) regarding judicial separation for failure to consummate. The school treats them differently based on the permanence of the defect. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying the correct ruling in marriage dissolution cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of husbands
Distinguish between a eunuch (majbub) and an impotent man ('anin). The eunuch has a permanent physical defect; the impotent may recover.
2
Determine the ruling for each
For the eunuch: immediate separation upon wife's demand. For the impotent: one-year delay to see if he recovers.
This is the Zahir al-Riwayah position.
3
Identify the underlying cause (illah)
The illah for immediate separation is the permanent inability; for the delayed, the potential for recovery.
This is derived from istihsan and custom.
4
Apply the conditions for separation
If the wife is a minor, wait for her puberty. The guardian may bring evidence of her satisfaction to prevent separation.
Also, the wife may demand an oath.
5
Note the exception for insanity
If the husband is insane, no delay is given because insanity does not affect sexual desire.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق باب العنين وغيره
بالمرأة من لها حق المطالبة بالجماع لأنها لو كانت صغيرة انتظر بلوغها في المجبوب والعنين لاحتمال رضاها بخلاف ما لو كان أحدهما مجنوناً فإنه لا يؤخر إلى عقله في الجب والعنة لعدم الفائدة ويفرق بينهما للحال في الجب، وبعد التأجيل في العنين لأن الجنون لا يعدم الشهوة بخصومة ولي إن كان وإلا فمن ينصبه القاضي. ولو جاء الولي ببينة في المسألتين على رضاها بعنته أو جبه أو على علمها بحاله عند العقد لم يفرق ولو طلب يمينها على ذلك تحلف، فإن نكلت لم يفرق وإن حلفت فرق؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وقالوا: لو جاءت امرأة المجبوب بولد بعد التفريق إلى سنتين يثبت نسبه ولا يبطل التفريق بخلاف العنين حيث يبطل التفريق لأنه لما ثبت نسبه لم يبق عنيناً. ونظر فيه الشارح بأن الطلاق وقع بتفريقه. وهو بائن فكيف يبطل ألا ترى أنها لو أقرت بعد التفريق أنه كان قد وصل اليها لا يبطل التفريق. وجوابه أن ثبوت النسب من المجبوب باعتبار الإنزال بالسحق والتفريق بينهما باعتبار الجب وهو موجود بخلاف ثبوته من العنين فإنه يظهر به أنه ليس بعنين والتفريق باعتباره بخلاف ما استشهد به من إقرارها فإنها متهمة في إبطال القضاء لاحتمال كذبها فظهر أن البحث بعيد كما في فتح القدير. وفي الخانية من فصل العنين: إذا شهد شاهدان بعد تفريق القاضي على إقرار المرأة قبل التفريق أنه وصل إليها يبطل تفريق القاضي، ولو أقرت بعد التفريق أنه قد وصل إليها لم تصدق على إبطال تفريق القاضي. اهـ. والحاصل أن تفريق القاضي في العنين يبطل بمجيء الولد وإقامة البينة على إقرارها بالوصول وفي التتارخانية: كان الزوج محبوباً ولم تعلم بحاله فجاءت بولد فادعاه وأثبت القاضي نسبه ثم علمت بحاله وطلبت الفرقة فلها ذلك اهـ.
Book of Divorce, Chapter on the Impotent and Others: The wife has the right to demand intercourse. If she is a minor, her reaching puberty is awaited for the eunuch and the impotent man due to the possibility of her satisfaction, unlike if one of them is insane, for then it is not delayed until his sanity in the case of the eunuch and the impotent due to lack of benefit. And they are separated immediately for the eunuch and after a delay for the impotent, because insanity does not eliminate desire. There is a lawsuit of a guardian if he exists, otherwise someone appointed by the judge. If the guardian brings evidence in both matters of her satisfaction with his impotence or eunuch status, or of her knowledge of his condition at the time of the contract, no separation occurs. And if she demands an oath on that, she swears; if she refuses, no separation; if she swears, separation occurs. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And they said: If the wife of a eunuch brings a child after separation up to two years, his lineage is established and the separation is not nullified, unlike the impotent where the separation is nullified because when his lineage is established, he is no longer impotent. The commentator objected that the divorce occurred by his separation, and it is a bain divorce, so how can it be nullified? Do you not see that if she acknowledged after separation that he had reached her, the separation is not nullified? The answer is that the establishment of lineage from a eunuch is due to ejaculation through rubbing (sahq), and the separation between them is due to his castration, which exists, unlike its establishment from the impotent, for it shows that he is not impotent, and the separation is based on that, unlike the analogy to her admission, because she is accused of invalidating the ruling due to the possibility of her lie. Thus it appears that the research is far-fetched, as in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Khaniyah, from the section on the impotent: If two witnesses testify after the judge's separation to the wife's admission before separation that he had reached her, the judge's separation is nullified. And if she admits after separation that he had reached her, she is not believed to invalidate the judge's separation. End. The summary is that the judge's separation in the case of an impotent man is nullified by the arrival of a child and by establishing evidence of her admission of reaching. And in al-Tatarkhaniyah: If the husband was a eunuch and she did not know his condition, and she brought a child and he claimed it and the judge established his lineage, then she knew his condition and demanded separation, she has that right. End.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and intra-madhhab discussion regarding the distinction between a eunuch (majbub) and an impotent man ('anin) in the context of judicial separation due to incapacity to consummate. The author begins by stating that a wife has the right to demand intercourse. If she is a minor, her reaching puberty is awaited for both categories, as she might be satisfied later. However, if one spouse is insane, the delay is not granted because insanity does not remove sexual desire. The immediate separation for a eunuch is based on the permanent physical defect, while the impotent man is given a one-year delay because he might recover. The guardian's role and evidentiary procedures are outlined: if the guardian proves the wife's satisfaction or her prior knowledge, no separation occurs; otherwise, she may seek it via oath or testimony. The key distinction then arises: if a eunuch's wife bears a child within two years after separation, the child's lineage is established but the separation remains valid, whereas for an impotent man, such a child nullifies the separation because it proves he is not impotent. The commentator (al-Sharih) critiques this by arguing that a bain divorce should not be reversible, but the response clarifies that the nullification is based on the underlying cause: for the eunuch, the defect remains even with a child (since the child could result from rubbing/sahq), whereas for the impotent, a child proves he is not truly impotent. Additional rulings from al-Khaniyah and al-Tatarkhaniyah confirm that evidence of the wife's prior admission or the birth of a child can nullify the separation only for the impotent, not for the eunuch.

Key Terms
المجبوب (al-majbub): A man whose penis has been completely cut off or is so short that he cannot penetrate at all.
العنين (al-'anin): A man who is impotent and cannot achieve an erection, but may recover.
التفريق (al-tafriq): Judicial separation due to defect, considered one bain divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a wife who demands separation from a eunuch husband?
A) She must wait one year before separation.
B) She is separated immediately.
C) She is separated only if she proves the defect in court.
D) She cannot seek separation because the marriage is valid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school treats a eunuch with immediate separation due to permanent defect, while an impotent man is given a one-year delay because recovery is possible.

The Effect of a Child Born After Separation: Eunuch vs. Impotent
Expansion probe: the effect of a child on separation for eunuch and impotent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a child born after separation nullifies the separation for an impotent man but not for a eunuch, and evaluate the Hanafi rationale.

Core Idea
A child does not nullify separation for a eunuch because child can be through rubbing; it does for an impotent because child proves he is not impotent.

This lesson addresses a nuanced issue: if a wife bears a child after judicial separation from a eunuch or an impotent husband, does the separation remain valid? Hanafi jurists differentiate based on the underlying cause of the defect. We will examine the proof, the critique from later scholars, and the response.

Guided Path
1
Understand the general rule
The birth of a child after separation can potentially prove that the husband is capable of consummation.
2
Apply to the eunuch
A eunuch can produce a child through rubbing (sahq) without penetration, so his defect remains. The separation stands.
The child's lineage is still established to avoid bastardy.
3
Apply to the impotent man
An impotent man's child proves he is not truly impotent; the basis for separation disappears. The separation is nullified.
This is based on the 'illah of temporary inability.
4
Consider the objection
Some scholars argued that a bain divorce should be final and not reversible. The Hanafi response: the nullification is based on the underlying cause, not the divorce itself.
The wife's admission after separation is not trusted, but a child is objective proof.
5
Review additional rulings
From al-Khaniyah: witnesses can nullify the separation if they testify to the wife's admission before separation. From al-Tatarkhaniyah: a wife who discovers later that her husband was a eunuch may still seek separation despite a child.
These support the distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

العنين (al-'anin): A man who is impotent and cannot achieve an erection, but may recover.
السحق (al-sahq): Rubbing or friction without penetration, which can cause ejaculation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A eunuch's wife bears a child one year after judicial separation. What is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The separation is nullified because the child proves ability to penetrate.
B) The separation remains valid, but the child's lineage is established.
C) The separation is nullified only if the child is born within one year.
D) The separation becomes a raj'i divorce.

Key Takeaway
A child born after separation nullifies the separation for an impotent man but not for a eunuch, based on the 'illah of permanence vs. treatability.

Conditions for Wife to Seek Separation from Eunuch
Lists conditions for the wife and the method of examining the husband's defect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a wife can seek separation from a eunuch and explain the procedure for examining the husband's defect.

Core Idea
A wife's right to separation depends on her being free and not imperforate; a slave woman's right is controlled by her master.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the conditions that qualify a wife to seek judicial separation from a husband who is a eunuch (majbub). It also addresses the special case of a slave wife and details the method of examining the husband to confirm his condition. Understanding these conditions is crucial for both the wife's legal standing and the court's procedure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qualifications of the wife
List the two main conditions: she must not be imperforate (ratqa') and she must be free. Note that the slave woman case differs.
2
Understand the dispute regarding the slave woman
Note the ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa gives choice to master, Abu Yusuf to the slave woman, Muhammad's position is disputed.
3
Recognize the effect of delay
The wife does not lose her option even if she stays with him for a time.
4
Describe the examination procedure
The court may examine by touch over clothing or, if necessary, by looking at the private part via a trusted person due to necessity.
5
Summarize the legal implications
The separation requires judicial decree after verifying conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأطلق في المرأة ولا بد من تقييدها بأن لا تكون رتقاء فإن الرتقاء إذا وجدته مجبوباً لا خيار لها كما في الخانية، وأن تكون حرة لأن زوج الأمة إذا كان محبوباً أو عنيناً فالخيار إلى المولى في قول أبي حنيفة، فإن رضي المولى لا حق للأمة، وإن لم يرض كانت الخصومة له كما في العزل. وقال أبو يوسف: الخيار إلى الأمة كقوله في العزل واختلفوا في قول محمد فقيل مع أبي يوسف كما في العزل، وقيل مع الإمام هنا؛ كذا في الخانية. ولم يقيد التفريق بالطلب للحال لأنها لو وجدته مجبوناً فأقامت معه زماناً وهو يضاجعها كانت على خيارها، ولم يذكر حكم ما إذا اختلفا في كونه محبوباً. وحكمه أنه إذا كان يعرف حقيقة حاله بالمس من غير نظر يمس من وراء الثياب ولا تكشف عورته، وإن كان لا يعرف إلا بالنظر أمر القاضي أميناً لينظر إلى عورته فيخبر بحاله لأن النظر إلى العورة يباح عند الضرورة؛ كذا في الخانية.
And the mention of the woman is absolute but must be qualified that she is not an imperforate woman (ratqa'), for the imperforate woman, if she finds him a eunuch, has no choice, as in al-Khaniyah. And that she be free, because the husband of a slave woman, if he is a eunuch or impotent, the choice belongs to the master according to Abu Hanifa. If the master is pleased, the slave woman has no right; if he is not pleased, the lawsuit belongs to him, as in the case of withdrawal. And Abu Yusuf said: The choice belongs to the slave woman, like his opinion in withdrawal. And they differed about the opinion of Muhammad: it is said he is with Abu Yusuf as in withdrawal, and it is said he is with the Imam here. Thus in al-Khaniyah. And the separation is not restricted to immediate request because if she finds him a eunuch and stays with him for some time while he is intimate with her, she retains her choice. And he did not mention the ruling if they differ about whether he is a eunuch. Its ruling is that if his true condition can be known by touch without looking, he is touched from behind the clothes and his private part is not uncovered; and if it cannot be known except by looking, the judge orders a trustworthy person to look at his private part and inform of his condition, because looking at the private part is permitted in necessity. Thus in al-Khaniyah.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
Here the author qualifies the general statement about the wife's right to seek separation by specifying conditions related to her. First, she must not be an imperforate woman (ratqa'), because if she is physically unable to be penetrated, she has no right to complain. Second, she must be free, because a slave woman's master has the right to decide, following Abu Hanifa's view that the master's consent is needed; Abu Yusuf holds that the slave woman herself has the choice, similar to his view on withdrawal (where the slave woman can object). There is a difference of opinion on Muhammad al-Shaybani's position, with some attributing to him agreement with Abu Yusuf. Additionally, the wife does not lose her option by delaying her request, even if she stays with him for a time and he is intimate with her (without full intercourse). The passage also details the method of examining the husband to determine if he is a eunuch: if possible, physical touch over the clothes without uncovering his private part; if necessary, the judge appoints a trustworthy person to look at his private part, as necessity permits such viewing.

Key Terms
الرتقاء (al-ratqa'): A woman with an imperforate vagina, such that intercourse is physically impossible.
الأمة (al-ummah): A slave woman.
الخصومة (al-khusuma): Lawsuit or claim; here it refers to bringing the case to court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, in a case where a slave woman's husband is a eunuch, who has the right to demand separation?
A) The slave woman herself.
B) The slave woman's master.
C) Both the woman and the master together.
D) No one, because the marriage is void.

Key Takeaway
The wife's right to separate from a eunuch is conditional upon her being free and not imperforate; slave women depend on their master's consent, and the court must properly examine the husband.

Eunuch vs Impotent: The One Quality Difference
Summarizes the distinction and additional rulings for eunuch and impotent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the single difference between the eunuch and the impotent in Hanafi law and identify the ruling for each.

Core Idea
The eunuch is separated immediately; the impotent is given a one-year delay.

This passage summarizes the key distinction between a eunuch (majbub) and an impotent man ('anin). While both defects prevent consummation, the Hanafi school treats them differently: a eunuch is separated right away, while an impotent man receives a year's delay to see if he can perform. The passage also adds three supplementary rulings regarding child birth, puberty, and health.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two defects
Recognize that the text discusses the eunuch (whose penis is cut or testicles removed) and the impotent (who cannot achieve erection). Note the common ruling for both: a bain divorce upon separation.
The passage clarifies that the type of divorce for the eunuch is the same as for the impotent.
2
Locate the one quality difference
The text states 'the impotent is given a delay and the eunuch is not'. Understand that this is the sole distinction: the impotent gets a one-year waiting period; the eunuch does not.
The delay is to determine if impotence can be overcome; the eunuch's defect is considered permanent.
3
Note the additional rulings
Three additional points are mentioned: (i) separation is nullified if a child is born, (ii) if the eunuch is a minor, we do not wait for him to reach puberty, (iii) the eunuch's health is not a condition for separation.
These rulings apply only when the husband has not consummated the marriage even once.
4
Understand the conditions for applicability
These rulings apply only if the husband is adult, healthy, and has never consummated; and the wife must be free, adult, not imperforate, not a slave, unaware before marriage, and not satisfied after.
These conditions are reiterated in the passage and apply to both defects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يذكر المصنف صفة الفرقة هنا اكتفاء بما ذكره في العنين وهو طلاق بائن كفرقة العنين كما في الخانية. والحاصل أن المجبوب كالعنين إلا في خصلة واحدة وهي أن العنين يؤجل والمجبوب لا؛ كذا في التتارخانية. ويزاد مسألة بطلان التفريق بمجيء الولد كما قد عملت. والثالثة لا ينتظر بلوغه. والرابعة لا تشترط صحته وفي فتح القدير: وما نقل عن الهندواني أنه يؤتى بطست فيه ماء بارد فيجلس فيه العنين فإن تلقص ذكره وانزوى علم أنه لا عنة به وإلا علم أنه عنين، لو اعتبر هذا لزم أن لا يؤجل سنة لأن التأجيل ليس إلا ليعرف أنه عنين على ما قالوا إذ لا فائدة فيه إن أجل مع ذلك لكن التأجيل لا بد منه لأنه حكمه اهـ. والحاصل أن طلبها التفريق في العنين له شرائط مختصة بهما فالمختص به أن يكون الزوج بالغاً صحيحاً لم يصل إليها مرة فالصبي لا يؤجل إلا بعد بلوغه والمريض بعد صحته والمختص بها أن تكون حرة بالغة غير رتقاء وقناء غير عالمة بحاله قبل النكاح وغير راضية به بعده. قوله: (وأجل سنة لو عنينا أو خصيا وهو من نزع خصيتاه وبقي ذكره وهو بفتح الخاء فعيل بمعنى مفعول مثل جريح وقتيل والجمع خصيان والخصيتان بالتاء البيضتان الواحدة خصية وبدون التاء الخصيان الجلدتان وجمع الخصية خُصي كمدية ومدى. وخصيت العبد أخصيه خصاء بالكسر والمد سللت خصيته وخصيت الفرس قطعت ذكره فهو مخصي، ويجوز استعمال فعيل ومفعول فيهما؛ كذا في المصباح ولا فرق هنا بين سلهما وقطعهما إذا كان ذكره لا ينتشر. قيدنا به لأن آلته لو كانت تنتشر لا خيار لها كما في المحيط، وعلى هذا لا حاجة إلى عطفه على العنين لأنه إن لم يكن عنيناً فلا تأجيل وإلا فهو داخل فيه ولذا لم يصرح بالخنثى الذي يبول من مبال الرجال والصبي الذي بلغ أربع عشرة سنة والشيخ الكبير وحكم الثلاث التأجيل كالعنين كما في الخانية لدخول الكل تحت اسم العنين. قال في الخانية: يؤجل الشيخ الكبير إن كان لا يصل إليها. اهـ. والمراد من المؤجل الحاكم ولا عبرة المذكورة عند الكرخي، وكذا الصغير المجبوب لكن تقدم في باب نكاح الكافر ما قد ينافي ذلك. التفريق بينه وبين زوجته بإبائه عن الإسلام لو عاقلاً أو إباء وليه وهذا التفريق طلاق.
And the author did not mention the description of the separation here, relying on what he mentioned for the impotent, which is a bain divorce, like the separation of the impotent, as in al-Khaniyah. The summary is that the eunuch is like the impotent except in one quality: that the impotent is given a delay and the eunuch is not. Thus in al-Tatarkhaniyah. And an additional issue is the nullification of separation by the arrival of a child, as you have learned. And the third: his reaching puberty is not waited for. And the fourth: his health is not required. And in Fath al-Qadir: What has been narrated from al-Hindwani that a basin of cold water is brought and the impotent sits in it; if his penis shrinks and retracts, it is known that he has no impotence, otherwise it is known that he is impotent. If this was considered, it would necessitate that he not be given a year's delay, because the delay is only to know if he is impotent, as they said, since there is no benefit if he is delayed with that, but the delay is necessary because it is his ruling. End. The summary is that her request for separation in the case of the impotent has conditions specific to both: specific to him is that the husband be adult, healthy, and has not reached her once; so a minor is not given a delay except after puberty, and a sick person after health. Specific to her is that she be free, adult, not imperforate, nor a slave, unaware of his condition before marriage, and not satisfied with it after. His statement: (And a delay of a year if he is impotent or castrated) and a castrated man is one whose testicles have been removed while his penis remains. It is with a fatha on the kha', a fa'il in the sense of maf'ul like jarih and qatil. The plural is khusyan. The testicles (with ta') are the two white things, each is a khisya; without ta', the khisyan are the two skins. The plural of khisya is khisi like mudiya and mudi. And you cause castration to a slave, I castrate him, khusa'an with kasr and madd means I extirpated his testicle; you castrate a horse means you cut his penis; so he is makhsi. It is permissible to use fa'il and maf'ul for both. Thus in al-Misbah. And there is no difference here between extracting them and cutting them if his penis does not become erect. We have restricted it by this because if his organ were to become erect, she would have no choice, as in al-Muhit. On this, there is no need to conjoin it with the impotent, because if he is not impotent, there is no delay, otherwise he is included in it. For this reason, he did not explicitly mention the hermaphrodite who urinates from the male urethra, the boy who has reached fourteen years, and the very old man. The ruling of all three is delay like the impotent, as in al-Khaniyah, because all enter under the term 'anin. Al-Khaniyah said: The very old man is given a delay if he cannot reach her. End. And what is intended by 'the one who is given a delay' is the judge; and there is no regard for the mentioned [condition] according to al-Karkhi. Similarly, the young eunuch, but it has preceded in the chapter on marriage of the disbeliever what may contradict that. And the separation between him and his wife due to his refusal of Islam if he is sane, or the refusal of his guardian, and this separation is a divorce.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage summarizes and expands upon the rulings for the eunuch (majbub) and the impotent ('anin). First, it notes that the author (al-Kanz) did not explicitly state the type of separation for the eunuch, but it is the same as for the impotent: a single bain divorce. The core difference is that the impotent is given a one-year delay, while the eunuch is separated immediately. Additional points: the nullification of separation by the birth of a child only applies to the impotent (as previously discussed); for the eunuch, puberty is not awaited (since he is already adult? Actually it says 'the third: his reaching puberty is not waited for' – this likely refers to the minor eunuch? But the context is unclear; it may mean that for a eunuch who is a minor, we do not wait for his puberty because the defect is permanent); and his health is not required (i.e., the eunuch does not need to be healthy for separation). A test from al-Hindwani is described: immersing the impotent in cold water; if his penis shrinks, he is not impotent; but the commentator dismisses this as overriding the necessity of the one-year delay, because the delay itself is the ruling. The conditions for the wife seeking separation are reiterated: the husband must be adult, healthy, and have never consummated; the wife must be free, adult, not imperforate, not a slave, unaware before marriage, and not satisfied after. Then a lexical explanation of 'khasi' (a castrated man) is given: one whose testicles are removed but penis remains. The ruling applies if the penis does not become erect. If it does erect, the wife has no choice. Also included under the same delay rule are a hermaphrodite with male urination, a boy of fourteen, and a very old man, all as types of impotence. Finally, a note about separation due to refusal of Islam: it is a divorce (bain).

Key Terms
المجبوب (al-majbub): A man whose penis is cut off or removed.
العنين (al-'anin): A man who is impotent, unable to achieve or maintain an erection.
الخصلة (al-khisla): A quality or characteristic; here the single difference between eunuch and impotent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The eunuch is given a one-year delay; the impotent is separated immediately.
B) Both are separated immediately.
C) The impotent is given a one-year delay; the eunuch is separated immediately.
D) Both are given a one-year delay.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between permanent and curable sexual defects: the eunuch is separated immediately, while the impotent receives a one-year delay.

Conditions and Extended Rulings for Separation Due to Impotence
Expands on conditions, test, lexical definitions, and inclusion of other cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the conditions required for a wife to seek separation due to impotence and identify which other persons (hermaphrodite, boy, old man) are given the same delay.

Core Idea
The wife's right to separation has strict conditions; persons with similar inability are treated like the impotent.

This passage expands on the conditions for the wife's request for separation and includes other cases that are analogized to the impotent. It also discusses a test for impotence and the ruling of separation due to apostasy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions for the wife's request
The text lists conditions specific to the husband (adult, healthy, never consummated) and specific to the wife (free, adult, not imperforate, not a slave, unaware of defect before marriage, and not satisfied after).
If any condition is missing, the wife cannot demand separation.
2
Analyze the test for impotence from al-Hindwani
A basin of cold water is brought; if the penis shrinks, the man is not impotent. The commentator criticizes this test because it would eliminate the need for the one-year delay.
The Hanafi school still requires the one-year delay regardless of such tests.
3
Recognize the lexical definition of 'khasi'
A khasi is one whose testicles are removed but penis remains. The ruling applies only if the penis does not become erect. If it does, the wife has no choice.
The text distinguishes between extracting and cutting testicles – both are treated the same.
4
Note the inclusion of other persons
A hermaphrodite who urinates from the male urethra, a boy who has reached fourteen, and a very old man are all given the same one-year delay as the impotent because they are all considered 'anin in the broad sense.
The eunuch (without erection) is also included, but the text clarifies that the castrated man with erection is not.
5
Understand separation due to apostasy
If a husband refuses to accept Islam (or his guardian refuses for him), separation occurs and it is a divorce.
This is a separate ground for separation, not directly related to impotence.

And you cause castration to a slave, I castrate him, khusa'an with kasr and madd means I extirpated his testicle; you castrate a horse means you cut his penis; so he is makhsi. It is permissible to use fa'il and maf'ul for both. Thus in al-Misbah. And there is no difference here between extracting them and cutting them if his penis does not become erect. We have restricted it by this because if his organ were to become erect, she would have no choice, as in al-Muhit. On this, there is no need to conjoin it with the impotent, because if he is not impotent, there is no delay, otherwise he is included in it. For this reason, he did not explicitly mention the hermaphrodite who urinates from the male urethra, the boy who has reached fourteen years, and the very old man. The ruling of all three is delay like the impotent, as in al-Khaniyah, because all enter under the term 'anin. Al-Khaniyah said: The very old man is given a delay if he cannot reach her. End. And what is intended by 'the one who is given a delay' is the judge; and there is no regard for the mentioned [condition] according to al-Karkhi. Similarly, the young eunuch, but it has preceded in the chapter on marriage of the disbeliever what may contradict that. And the separation between him and his wife due to his refusal of Islam if he is sane, or the refusal of his guardian, and this separation is a divorce.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage summarizes and expands upon the rulings for the eunuch (majbub) and the impotent ('anin). First, it notes that the author (al-Kanz) did not explicitly state the type of separation for the eunuch, but it is the same as for the impotent: a single bain divorce. The core difference is that the impotent is given a one-year delay, while the eunuch is separated immediately. Additional points: the nullification of separation by the birth of a child only applies to the impotent (as previously discussed); for the eunuch, puberty is not awaited (since he is already adult? Actually it says 'the third: his reaching puberty is not waited for' – this likely refers to the minor eunuch? But the context is unclear; it may mean that for a eunuch who is a minor, we do not wait for his puberty because the defect is permanent); and his health is not required (i.e., the eunuch does not need to be healthy for separation). A test from al-Hindwani is described: immersing the impotent in cold water; if his penis shrinks, he is not impotent; but the commentator dismisses this as overriding the necessity of the one-year delay, because the delay itself is the ruling. The conditions for the wife seeking separation are reiterated: the husband must be adult, healthy, and have never consummated; the wife must be free, adult, not imperforate, not a slave, unaware before marriage, and not satisfied after. Then a lexical explanation of 'khasi' (a castrated man) is given: one whose testicles are removed but penis remains. The ruling applies if the penis does not become erect. If it does erect, the wife has no choice. Also included under the same delay rule are a hermaphrodite with male urination, a boy of fourteen, and a very old man, all as types of impotence. Finally, a note about separation due to refusal of Islam: it is a divorce (bain).

Key Terms
الرتقاء (al-ratqa'): A woman who is imperforate (closed vagina) and thus cannot be penetrated.
القناء (al-qana'): A slave woman (female slave).
الخنثى (al-khuntha): A hermaphrodite; here one who urinates from the male urethra.
المؤجل (al-mu'ajjal): The one who is given a delay; here refers to the judge who imposes the delay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following persons is NOT given a one-year delay like the impotent?
A) A hermaphrodite who urinates from the male urethra.
B) A boy who has reached fourteen years and cannot consummate.
C) A very old man who cannot consummate.
D) A castrated man whose penis becomes erect.

Key Takeaway
The right to separation due to impotence has strict conditions for both spouses, and the delay applies to all who are unable to consummate regardless of age or gender ambiguity.

Talaq — Divorce

The Impotent Husband: Intra-Hanafi Dispute and Conditions for Separation
Explaining rulings for impotent, castrated, and emasculated husbands with intra-Hanafi differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on postponement for an impotent husband, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a slave-girl's right to separation, and list the conditions required for a wife to seek separation.

Core Idea
A wife's right to separation for impotence requires a year's postponement by a judge, and the slave-girl's right is disputed between Abu Hanifah and his students.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq expands on the rulings concerning an impotent (ʿannīn), castrated (khaṣī), and emasculated (majbūb) husband. It presents the core legal framework of a one-year postponement before separation, and then delves into an intra-Hanafi ikhtilāf regarding a slave-girl's standing in such cases. Understanding these details is essential for correctly advising on marital dissolutions due to physical defects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The passage begins by stating that the judge imposes a one-year postponement; if intercourse occurs, no separation, otherwise irrevocable divorce upon a second request.
The postponement is only by a judge of a major city.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on the slave-girl
Examine the positions of Abu Hanifah (master's right) vs. Abu Yusuf and possibly Muhammad (slave-girl's right). Note the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).
The dispute is analogous to the case of ʿazl (coitus interruptus).
3
List the conditions for the wife's right
The wife must be free, adult, not ratqā (obstructed vagina), unaware of impotence at marriage, and not consenting afterwards; the husband must be adult, healthy, and have never consummated.
These conditions are specific to the impotent case.
4
Understand the postponement procedure and evidence
The postponement must be by a judge of a metropolis or city, the year is lunar in ẓāhir al-riwāya, and the evidence is the practice of the four Caliphs.
The solar year (365 days) is the basis for fatwa according to al-Khulāṣa, but the lunar year (354) is the relied-upon position.

الهندواني أنه يؤتى بطست فيه ماء بارد فيجلس فيه العنين فإن تلقص ذكره وانزوى علم أنه لا عنة به وإلا علم أنه عنين، لو اعتبر هذا لزم أن لا يؤجل سنة لأن التأجيل ليس إلا ليعرف أنه عنين على ما قالوا إذ لا والمعتوه إذا زوجه وليه امرأة فلم يصل إليها أجله القاضي سنة بحضرة الخصم عنه ولا بد من تقييد الزوج بكونه صحيحاً كما سيأتي أن المريض لا يؤجل حتى يصح ولم يذكره محمد. تلك واختلفوا في السنة فقيل شمسية وهي (فإن وطئ وإلا بانت بالتفريق إن طلبت أي طلباً ثانياً فالأول للتأجيل والثاني للتفريق. وذكر خجامسكين أن قوله إن طلبت متعلق بالجميع وهو حسن وطلب وكيلها بالتفريق عند غيبتها كطلبها على خلاف فيه ولم يذكره محمد وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا طلبت على باب أنه : كائناً كان قوله : (لا يكون إلا عند قاضي مصر أو مدينة قال الرملي ومن في معناه كالمحكم فسيأتي في يصح حكمه في غير حد وقود فيشمل التأجيل المذكور وغيره ولو مع وجود القاضي لإطلاقهم تأمل . ا هـ . ويخالفه ما في الفتح حيث قال : ولا يعتبر تأجيل غير الحاكم . من وفي الولوالجية : ولا يكون إلا عند القاضي لأن هذا مقدمة أمر لا يكون إلا عند القاضي وهو الفرقة فكذا مقدمته قوله : (قال) في الخلاصة وعليه الفتوى قال في الفتح : اختاره شمس الأئمة اهـ.
He gave a separation immediately and a postponement of one year for the impotent or castrated man. Then if he has intercourse, [no separation]; otherwise, she becomes separated by the separation if she requests, regarding the master according to Abu Hanifa: if the master agrees, the slave-girl has no right; if he does not agree, the dispute is his, as in the case of isolation. Abu Yusuf said: The choice is the slave-girl's, like his statement regarding isolation. And they differed regarding Muhammad's statement: it is said he is with Abu Yusuf, as in isolation; and it is said he is with the Imām here; thus in al-Khāniyya. He did not restrict the separation to immediate request, because if she finds him emasculated and stays with him for a time while he has intercourse with her, she retains her option. He did not mention the ruling when they differ about whether he is [truly] impotent. Its ruling: if his condition can be known by touch without looking, he is touched from behind clothes and his private part is not uncovered; if it is known only by looking, the judge orders a trustworthy man to look at his private part and inform him of his condition, because looking at the private part is permitted in necessity; thus in al-Khāniyya. The author did not mention the type of separation here, relying on what he mentioned in the case of the impotent, which is an irrevocable divorce like the separation of the impotent, as in al-Khāniyya. The summary is that the emasculated is like the impotent except in one matter: the impotent is given a postponement, the emasculated is not; thus in al-Tatārkhāniyya. An additional issue: the invalidity of separation by the arrival of a child as has been practiced. The third: he is not waited until his attainment of majority. The fourth: his health is not a condition. And in Fatḥ al-Qadīr: what was transmitted from al-Hindawānī that a basin with cold water is brought, and the impotent sits in it; if his penis shrinks and retracts, it is known he is not impotent; otherwise he is impotent. If this were considered, it would necessitate not postponing for a year, because postponement is only to determine if he is impotent, as they said, since there is no benefit if he is postponed despite that, but postponement is inevitable because it is its ruling. And the summary is that her request for separation in the case of impotence has conditions specific to each. The condition specific to him: that the husband be an adult, healthy, and has never had intercourse with her. So a minor is not postponed except after adulthood, a patient after health. The conditions specific to her: that she be a free, adult woman, not a rātiqa (having impenetrable vagina) nor a qarnā (having a bony protrusion), not aware of his condition before marriage, and not satisfied with it after. His statement: (And he is given a postponement of one year if [the husband] is a castrated or emasculated man) - and he is the one whose testicles have been removed and his penis remains. It is with a fatḥa on the khā, faʿīl in the meaning of mafʿūl, like jarīḥ and qatīl. The plural is khisyān. The khisyatān with a tā are the two testicles, singular khisya; without tā, al-khiṣyān are the two scrotums. The plural of khisya is khusiyy like midya and mady. And you say: khaṣaytu al-ʿabda akhṣīhi khaṣāan (with kasra and madd) meaning I removed his testicle; and khaṣaytu al-farasa means I cut off its penis, so it is makhṣiyy. Both faʿīl and mafʿūl are used; thus in al-Miṣbāḥ. There is no difference here between removing them and cutting them off if his organ does not become erect. We specify this because if his organ becomes erect, she has no option, as in al-Muḥīṭ. On this basis, there is no need to join it to the impotent because if he is not impotent, there is no postponement; otherwise he is included in it. Hence he did not explicitly mention the hermaphrodite who urinates from the male organ, the boy who has reached fourteen, and the old man. The ruling for all three is postponement like the impotent, as in al-Khāniyya, because all are included under the term 'impotent'. He said in al-Khāniyya: The old man is postponed if he cannot have intercourse with her. The one who does the postponement is the judge, and the postponement of others is not considered. He also said in al-Khāniyya: The postponement of the impotent is only before a judge of a metropolis or city, so neither the woman's postponement nor another's postponement is considered. Her consent before a non-judge nullifies her right, in al-Khulāṣa. If the judge is removed after he has postponed, the successor builds on the first postponement and begins the year from the time of the dispute. It is derived from the formulation of the issue that the marriage of the impotent is valid. If she knew of his impotence at the time of marriage, she has no option, just as if the buyer knew of the defect of the sold item. If she did not know at the time and came to know later, she has the right to dispute even if a long time has passed, as in al-Khāniyya. In al-Muḥīṭ: The Imāms followed in the rulings of the impotent are ʿUmar, ʿAlī, Ibn Masʿūd, and Ibn ʿAbbās (may Allah be pleased with them), and no opposition from their peers is reported, so it is like consensus. And because the lack of reaching may be due to a temporary cause or a permanent defect; so a period must be set to distinguish the cause from impotence. It was set as a year because it includes the four seasons. We have written in the legal maxims of the Hanafī school that if a judge ruled not to postpone the impotent, his ruling is not enforced, and the woman is not bound by anything. She must be free and not rātiqa, as we presented in the wife of the emasculated. The reason given in al-Ikhtiyār is that the rātiqa has no right to intercourse, so she cannot seek [separation]. If they differ about whether she is rātiqa, women examine her, as in al-Tatārkhāniyya. The author used the general term 'husband', so it includes the insane person, as in al-Khāniyya: If an insane person is married by his guardian to a woman and he cannot have intercourse with her, the judge postpones him for a year in the presence of the opponent. But the husband must be restricted to being healthy, as will come: the sick person is not postponed until he recovers. Muhammad did not mention this. They differed about the year: it is said it is a solar year, which exceeds the lunar by eleven days. In al-Khulāṣa: The fatwa is upon it. And it is said it is a lunar year, i.e., 354 days, and it was declared correct in al-Wāqiʿāt and al-Walwālijiyya, and it is the apparent narration (ẓāhir al-riwāya) as in al-Hidāya, so it is the relied-upon because it is established from the author of the school. In al-Khāniyya: If the lack of reaching is established, the judge postpones him whether he requests or not, and writes the postponement and witnesses the date. In al-Mujtabā: If the postponement occurs in the middle of the month, days are considered by consensus, as mentioned in the chapter on ʿidda. His statement: (Then if he has intercourse, otherwise she becomes separated by the separation if she requests) - meaning a second request; the first is for the postponement, the second for the separation. Khājamaskīn mentioned that his phrase 'if she requests' applies to all [i.e., both the postponement and the separation], and it is good. The request of her agent for separation in her absence is like her request, with disagreement on it; Muhammad did not mention it. And he (the author) used a general expression, so it includes if she requests in whatever manner. His statement: (It is only before a judge of a metropolis or city) - al-Ramlī said: and those like him, like an arbitrator, as will come in the chapter that his judgment is valid in other than ḥadd and qiṣāṣ, so it includes the mentioned postponement and others, even if a judge exists, by their general usage, reflect. This conflicts with what is in al-Fatḥ, where he said: The postponement of other than the judge is not considered. In al-Walwālijiyya: It is only before the judge because this is a preliminary matter that is only done before the judge, which is the separation, and similarly its preliminary. His statement: (He said) in al-Khulāṣa: The fatwa is upon it. He said in al-Fatḥ: Shams al-Aʾimma chose it.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq is an expansion on the rulings related to a husband who is impotent (ʿannīn), castrated (khaṣī), or emasculated (majbūb). The author opens by stating the general ruling: if a wife seeks separation due to impotence, the judge postpones the decision for one year. If the husband has intercourse within that year, the marriage continues; otherwise, the wife obtains an irrevocable separation (ṭalāq bāʾin) upon a second request. A key intra-Hanafi dispute is presented regarding a slave-girl (umma) married to an impotent man. According to Abu Hanifah, the right to demand separation belongs to the slave-girl's master, not the slave-girl herself. If the master consents, the slave-girl has no independent right; if he does not, he may bring the case. Abu Yusuf, however, holds that the choice belongs to the slave-girl herself, analogous to his position in the case of ʿazl (coitus interruptus) where she has a say. Muhammad's position is disputed; some say he agrees with Abu Yusuf, others with Abu Hanifah. The text then distinguishes between the emasculated and the truly impotent: the latter is given a year's postponement, while the former is not, since his condition is permanent. Several conditions for the wife's right to seek separation are listed: she must be free, adult, not rātiqa (with an obstructed vagina) or qarnā (with a growth), unaware of his condition at the time of marriage, and not consenting afterwards. For the husband, he must be an adult, healthy, and have never consummated the marriage. The postponement itself is only valid when ordered by a judge of a major city; the wife's own postponement or that of a non-judge is not considered. The duration of the postponement—one year—is a subject of disagreement: the solar year (365 days) is the basis for fatwa according to al-Khulāṣa, while the lunar year (354 days) is the relied-upon position (al-muʿtamad) because it is the apparent narration (ẓāhir al-riwāya). The evidence for this ruling is the consensus-like practice of the four Caliphs (ʿUmar, ʿAlī, Ibn Masʿūd, Ibn ʿAbbās) and the rationale that the year suffices to distinguish temporary causes from permanent impotence, as it covers all seasons.

Key Terms
العنين (al-ʿannīn): A man who is unable to achieve an erection or penetrate due to a physical defect, but whose condition may be temporary or treatable; he is given a one-year postponement.
الخصي (al-khaṣī): A man whose testicles have been removed (castrated) but whose penis remains; if his penis can become erect, he is not considered impotent; otherwise he is treated like the ʿannīn.
المجبوب (al-majbūb): A man whose penis has been amputated or removed; his condition is permanent, so no postponement is given; the wife has an immediate right to separation if unaware.
الرتقاء (al-ratqāʾ): A woman whose vagina is obstructed or impenetrable, preventing intercourse; such a woman has no right to claim separation due to her husband's impotence because she cannot benefit from the right.
بائن (bāʾin): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately without possibility of revocation; the couple cannot remarry without a new contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a slave-girl (umma) is married to an impotent man and her master does not want separation?
A) The slave-girl can still demand separation herself according to all Hanafi imams.
B) Abu Hanifah says the master has the right, so if the master refuses, the slave-girl cannot demand separation.
C) The marriage is automatically annulled after one year.
D) The slave-girl must wait until the master gives permission.

Key Takeaway
A wife's right to separation due to impotence requires a one-year postponement by a judge, and the slave-girl's right is disputed between Abu Hanifah (master's right) and Abu Yusuf (slave-girl's right).

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
12 min
Rulings on the Impotent Husband ('Anin)
Commentary on the 'anin's deferment, evidence, and wife's option.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for deferment of an 'anin and explain why the relied-upon year is lunar.

Core Idea
The impotent husband is given one lunar year to consummate; otherwise the wife may seek separation.

The Hanafi school rules that a marriage with an impotent husband is valid. If the wife discovers his condition after marriage, she may request a judge to defer him for one year to see if he can consummate. This ruling is based on the practice of leading Companions, which attained the status of consensus. There is an internal dispute over whether the year is solar or lunar; the relied-upon view is lunar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is the marriage of an impotent man. The ruling: the marriage is valid, and the wife has the option to seek a one-year deferment after which she may request separation if still not consummated.
The wife's right is established if she was unaware at marriage.
2
Locate the Dalil
The evidence is the practice of the Companions: 'Umar, 'Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ibn 'Abbas. Their agreement, with no recorded opposition, stands as consensus (ijma).
The ruling is based on a non-textual source but is authoritative.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The Companions set a one-year period to determine if the impotence is temporary or permanent. The year covers all four seasons, allowing for natural variation.
The 'illah is the need for a standard waiting period.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Scholars differ on whether the year is solar (365 days) or lunar (354 days). Some early fatwas favored solar, but the relied-upon view is lunar.
The practical difference is 11 days.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
The lunar year is chosen because it is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) from Abu Hanifa and aligns with Islamic practice using lunar months.
This is the mufta bihi position.

He said in al-Khaniyya also: The deferment of the impotent is only before a judge of Egypt or a city, so the deferment of the wife or others is not considered. End. As for her consent to it before a non-judge, it drops her right in al-Khulasa. If the judge is removed after he deferred him, the successor builds on the first deferment and begins the year from the time of the lawsuit. It is learned from the premise of the issue that the marriage of the impotent is valid; if she knew of his impotence at the time of marriage, she has no option, just as if the buyer knew of the defect of the item. If she did not know at the time and knew afterwards, she has the right to sue even if the time is long, as in al-Khaniyya. In al-Muhit: The imams followed in the rulings of the impotent are 'Umar, 'Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ibn 'Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them, and no opposition from their peers is transmitted, so it stands in place of consensus. Because the absence of reaching may be due to a temporary cause or a permanent defect, so a period must be set to distinguish the cause from impotence, so it was set as a year because it includes the four seasons. He reasoned it in al-Ikhtiyar that the ratqa' has no right to intercourse, so she does not possess the claim. If they dispute whether she is a ratqa', women examine her, as in al-Tatarakhaniyya. The husband is unqualified so it includes the mentally deficient, as in al-Khaniyya: If the guardian of a mentally deficient man marries him to a woman and he did not reach her, the judge defers him for a year in the presence of the opponent. Then they differed regarding the year: it was said solar, and it exceeds the lunar by eleven days. He said in al-Khulasa: Upon it is the fatwa. And it was said lunar, and it is three hundred and fifty-four days, and it was corrected in al-Waqi'at and al-Walayjaniyya, and it is the apparent narration as in al-Hidaya, so it is the relied-upon because it is established from the author of the school. In al-Khaniyya: If lack of reaching is established, the judge defers him whether he asks or not, and he writes the deferment and witnesses the date. In al-Mujtaba: If the deferment occurs in the middle of the month, it is considered by days by consensus, as mentioned in al-'Idda.
