Ponder. End. And it is opposed by what is in al-Fath where he said: The deferment of a non-judge is not considered. And in al-Wilwajiyya: It is only before a judge because this is a preliminary to a matter that is only before a judge, which is separation, so likewise its preliminary. His statement: (He said) in al-Khulasa: Upon it is the fatwa. He said in al-Fath: Shams al-A'imma chose it. End. Al-Bahr al-Raiq vol. 4 p. 14. Book of Divorce, Chapter on the Impotent and Others. So if he says 'I had intercourse' and she denies and they say she is a virgin, she is given the choice; if she is a thayyib, he is believed with his oath. If she chooses him, her right is void, and neither is given a choice due to a defect. With it, postponement first and second, so if she sued him then left for a period, she has the right to demand; even if she complied with him in sleeping those days, as in al-Khaniyya. Since this separation before actual consummation is irrevocable, she has the full mahr and must observe 'idda due to valid seclusion. And he indicated that if he had intercourse with her once, she has no right to demand because her right is dropped entirely judicially, and what is extra is valid de facto not de jure, as in Jami' Qadikhan. In his fatawa: If he was having intercourse with her but not in the vagina, until he ejaculates and she ejaculates, and he does not reach her vagina, and she persisted in that for a time, virgin or thayyib, then she sued him to the judge, he defers him a year. If he has intercourse after the deferment, her right drops even if she is menstruating, postpartum, fasting, or in ihram. Thus in al-Mi'raj. So too if the husband asks to defer after the year even one day, the judge does not grant him except with her consent, and she has the right to return and choose separation, thus in al-Ikhtiyar. We have presented that the intended wife is free; as for a slave, the option belongs to her master not her, like permission for 'azl. In al-Muhit: He divorced her then remarried her, she has no option because she consented to stay. If he marries another woman knowing his condition, she has no option, and upon it is the fatwa. If he had a wife with whom he had intercourse and she gave birth first, then he divorced her, then married her again and did not reach in the second marriage, he is impotent because with each contract her right to demand is renewed. End. In al-Mi'raj: A minor is qualified here for divorce in the issue of the amputated male organ because it is due upon him, just as the emancipation of a relative qualifies. And some made it a separation without divorce, and the first is more correct. End. With it, his statement: (So if he says 'I had intercourse' and she denies and they say she is a virgin, she is given the choice; if she is a thayyib, he is believed with his oath). He made it absolute so it includes if the dispute occurs in the beginning, by his claiming reaching her and she denying, or at the end. His statement 'she is given the choice' includes giving a choice to defer him a year at the beginning or to choose separation after deferment. The summary: if she is a thayyib, his word is believed regarding intercourse at beginning and end with his oath. If he refuses to swear at the beginning, he is deferred a year, and he is not deferred except if lack of reaching is established. If he refuses to swear at the end, she is given choice for separation. If she is a virgin, lack of reaching is established by their statement, so he is deferred at the beginning and separated at the end. By this it appears that what the commentator mentioned that the author did not mention the method of establishing impotence at the beginning and mentioned it at the end is a negligence of what I understood from his words, because we have established that giving choice includes both, and the restriction by his statement 'they say' in al-Sarakhsi, Qadikhan, and Zahir al-Din, and it is the narration of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa. His statement: (And it was said lunar) al-Fath said its evidence is what is established from the Companions like 'Umar and those we mentioned with him, as a statement, and the people of Islamic law are accustomed to months and years by the crescent moons. So when they absolutely say year, it refers to that unless they explicitly state otherwise. His statement: (On postponement first and second) meaning before the deferment and after, but will come in the request for separation a difference regarding restriction to the sitting. In some copies 'on postponement or not' with 'or' the coordinating conjunction and 'not' the negative, and this is more apparent. His statement: (She has no option, and upon it is the fatwa) (His statement: will come shortly from al-Khaniyya correction of its opposite, and its content will come).
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary (sharh) on the rulings concerning the impotent husband ('anin). The author, Imam Zayla'i, explains the conditions, evidence, and procedures. The text begins by establishing that the deferment of an 'anin must be ordered by a judge of a major city or capital, not by the wife or anyone else. If a non-judge grants a deferment, it is invalid. However, if the wife consents to a non-judicial deferment, she forfeits her right to later claim. If the judge who granted the deferment is removed, the successor judge continues from the same deferment, starting the year from the time of the initial complaint, not from the date of the judgment. The validity of the marriage is affirmed: if the wife knew of his impotence at the time of marriage, she has no option; if she did not know, she may sue even after a long time. The evidence for this ruling comes from the practice of the Companions 'Umar, 'Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ibn 'Abbas, which attained the status of consensus (ijma'). The rationale is that the inability to consummate may be temporary or permanent, so a waiting period of one year is set to discern the cause, as it covers all four seasons. The text then discusses conditions: the wife must be free (not a slave) and not affected by ratq (a physical obstruction preventing intercourse), as a ratqa' has no right to intercourse. If the husband is a lunatic (ma'tuh), his guardian can marry him, and he too is granted a year. The husband must be healthy; if he is sick, the deferment is postponed until he recovers. A significant ikhtilaf is presented regarding the definition of the year: some say it is a solar year (365 days), others a lunar year (354 days). The author notes that the fatwa is given on the solar year in al-Khulasa, but the relied-upon (mu'tamad) position is the lunar year, as it is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) and established from the school's founder (Abu Hanifa). The procedure: if the husband has intercourse during the year, the wife's right is dropped; if not, and she requests a second time after the year, the judge separates them. The wife's request for separation can be made through her agent, and she can exercise her option with delay. If the husband claims he had intercourse and the wife denies, the ruling depends on her status: if she is a virgin (bikr), her word (or that of women examining her) is taken, and she is given the choice; if she is a thayyib (non-virgin), the husband's word is taken with his oath. The separation is considered irrevocable (ba'in) if it occurs before actual consummation, and the wife is entitled to the full mahr and must observe 'idda due to valid seclusion. Once separation occurs, if she remarries him later with a new contract, she again has the right to demand if he fails to consummate, as each contract is independent.

Key Terms
العنين (al-'anin): A man who is unable to achieve vaginal penetration due to inherent impotence.
التأجيل (al-ta'jil): The one-year deferment granted by a judge to the 'anin to attempt consummation.
الرتقاء (al-ratqa'): A woman whose vagina is closed or obstructed, preventing intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (mu'tamad) opinion in the Hanafi school regarding the length of the deferment for an impotent husband?
A) Solar year (365 days)
B) Lunar year (354 days)
C) One full year from the marriage contract
D) Until the husband recovers

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school gives the impotent husband one lunar year to consummate; failure leads to separation at the wife's request, based on the practice of the Companions.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Wife's Claim of Impotence: Virgin vs. Non-Virgin
States the ruling on wife's credibility in impotence cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the wife's credibility in impotence cases and apply the distinction between virgin and non-virgin to determine the procedure and outcome.

Core Idea
A virgin wife's word is accepted; a non-virgin wife's word is not.

In cases of impotence (innah), a dispute often arises over whether consummation occurred. The Hanafi school distinguishes based on the wife's virginity status because virginity is an observable sign. This lesson explains the rule, the conditions for the wife's option, and the procedure of deferment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The husband claims he has consummated the marriage, but the wife denies. The legal question is whose word is accepted.
The wife must be claiming impotence as a defect.
2
Apply the credibility rule based on virginity
If the wife is a virgin (bikr), her word is accepted and she is given the option to demand a one-year deferment. If she is a non-virgin (thayyib), the husband's oath is accepted.
The distinction is based on the presumption that virginity supports the claim of non-consummation.
3
Describe the deferment procedure
The judge gives the husband one year to consummate. After the year, if no consummation occurs, the wife may demand separation (faskh), which is a final divorce (ba'in).
The deferment is immediate upon the wife's complaint.
4
Identify what nullifies the wife's right
One instance of actual intercourse (even during menses, fasting, etc.) nullifies her right. Also, if the wife knew of the impotence before marriage or consented afterward, her right is lost.
Consent is implied by remarriage or staying after knowledge.
5
Note special cases
For a slave wife, the option belongs to her master. A new marriage contract renews the right. A minor husband can be subject to the same ruling.
These exceptions are derived from the broader principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو قال وطئت وأنكرت وقلن بكر خيرت وإن كانت ثيباً صدق بحلفه وإن اختارته بطل حقها ولم يخير أحدهما بعيب . معه التراخي أولاً وثانياً ولذا لو خاصمته ثم تركت مدة فلها المطالبة ولو طاوعته في المضاجعة تلك الأيام كما في الخانية. ولما كانت هذه فرقة قبل الدخول حقيقة كانت بائنة ولها كمال المهر وعليها العدة لوجود الخلوة الصحيحة. وأشار إلى أنه لو وطئها مرة لا حق لها في المطالبة لسقوط حقها بالمرة قضاء وما زاد عليها فهو مستحق ديانة لا قضاء كما في جامع قاضيخان . وفي فتاواه : لو كان يأتيها فيما دون الفرج حتى ينزل وتنزل ولا يصل إليها في فرجها وقامت على ذلك زماناً وهي بكر أو ثيب ثم خاصمته إلى القاضي أجله القاضي سنة، ولو وطئها بعد التأجيل سقط حقها ولو حائضاً أو نفساء أو صائمة أو محرمة، كذا في المعراج وإلى أن الزوج لو طلب أن يؤجل بعد السنة ولو يوماً لا يجيبه القاضي إلا برضاها ولها الرجوع واختيار الفرقة ؛ كذا في الاختيار. وقدمنا أن المراد بالزوجة الحرة، أما الأمة فالخيار لمولاها لا لها كالإذن في العزل، وفي المحيط : فرق بينهما ثم تزوجها ثانياً لا خيار لها لرضاها بالمقام م ولو تزوج أخرى عالمة بحاله لا خيار لها وعليه الفتوى ولو كان له امرأة يصل إليها وولدت منه أولاً ثم أبانها ثم تزوجها ولم يصل في النكاح الثاني فهو عنين لأنها باعتبار كل عقد يتجدد لها حق المطالبة اهـ. وفي المعراج : ويؤهل الصبي هنا للطلاق في مسألة الجب لأنه مستحق عليه كما يؤهل بعتق القريب ومنم من جعله فرقة بغير طلاق والأول أصح اهـ.
If he says 'I have had intercourse' and she denies, and they say she is a virgin, she is given the option; if she is a non-virgin, he is believed on his oath. If she chooses him, her right is void. Neither is given an option due to a defect. With him, the deferment is immediate and also secondary. Therefore, if she litigates then leaves for a while, she still has the right to demand; even if she complies with him in lying together during those days, as in al-Khaniyah. And since this separation is before consummation in reality, it is a final separation, and she gets the full dower, and upon her is the waiting period due to valid seclusion. And he indicated that if he has intercourse with her once, she has no right to demand because her right is nullified completely in the judiciary, and what is beyond that is owed in conscience but not judicially, as in Jami' Qadikhan. And in his Fatawa: If he approaches her below the private part until he and she ejaculate, but does not reach her private part, and this continues for a time, she being virgin or non-virgin, then she litigates to the judge, he gives him a year. If he has intercourse after the deferment, her right falls, even if she is menstruating, postpartum, fasting, or in ihram. Similarly in al-Mi'raj. And that if the husband asks for a deferment after the year, even for a day, the judge does not respond to him except with her consent. She has the right to return and choose separation. Similarly in al-Ikhtiyar. And we have stated that the intended wife is free; as for the slave, the option is for her master, not for her, like permission for coitus interruptus. In al-Muhit: If he divorces her then remarries her, she has no option due to her consent to stay. And if he marries another knowing his condition, she has no option; this is the fatwa. And if he has a wife with whom he consummates and she bears from him, then he divorces her then remarries her but does not consummate in the second marriage, he is considered impotent because with each contract the right to demand is renewed for her. And in al-Mi'raj: The minor is considered eligible here for divorce in the issue of castration because it is owed upon him, just as he is considered eligible for manumission of a relative. And some make it a separation without divorce; the first is more correct.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter on the impotent husband. It addresses the dispute between husband and wife over whether consummation occurred. The author states the rule: if the wife is a virgin (bikr), her word is accepted because virginity is a visible sign; she is given the option to demand a deferment of one year. If she is a non-virgin (thayyib), the husband's claim is accepted upon oath. If she chooses to stay with him, her right to demand separation is void. The deferment period is immediate (upon complaint) and also later (after the year). The wife does not lose her right to demand by cooperating in bed during the deferment. The separation before consummation is a final divorce (ba'in), so the wife gets full dower and must observe 'iddah. One instance of intercourse nullifies her right judicially; additional acts have only spiritual obligation. The fatawa extend this: if he does not reach the private part but both orgasm, the husband still gets a year. Intercourse during any state (menses, postpartum, etc.) nullifies her right. The husband cannot get an extension beyond one year without her consent. The rule applies to free wives; for slave wives the option belongs to the master. If a woman remarries an impotent man knowing his condition, she loses her option. A new marriage contract renews the right. A minor husband who is castrated is eligible for the divorce ruling.

Key Terms
عَنه ('innah): Impotence; inability of the husband to have vaginal intercourse despite desire.
بِكر (bikr): A female who has not had sexual intercourse; virginity is established by intact hymen.
أَجمَل (ajala): To defer; the judge gives the husband one year to consummate or prove ability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The husband's oath is accepted, no deferment.
B) The wife's word is accepted, and she is given a year's deferment.
C) Both are believed, and they separate immediately.
D) The judge decides based on witnesses only.

Key Takeaway
A virgin wife's claim of non-consummation is believed, giving her the right to demand a one-year deferment and separation if no consummation occurs.

Wife's Choice and the Session Condition
Explains the effect of the wife's choice to stay and the condition of session

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the wife's implicit choice (standing/staying) and explain the session condition that voids her option.

Core Idea
Standing from the session without choosing is equivalent to choosing to stay, voiding her right to separation.

The wife's right to demand separation (khiyar) can be voided not only by explicit words but also by her actions. The session in which the judge presents the option is critical: any action indicating consent, such as standing up, implicitly cancels her option. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its intra-madhhab nuances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the wife's choice to stay (ikhtiyar) after being given the option to separate. The ruling is that her choice voids her right to demand separation.
This applies whether the choice is explicit or implicit.
2
Locate the implicit forms
Implicit choice includes standing up from the session, staying with her husband in compliance (e.g., lying together), or being made to stand by the judge's assistants.
These actions indicate consent even without words.
3
Understand the session condition
The option must be exercised in the same session. If the judge gives the option and she merely remains or stands without choosing, her option is void. Before the judge's option, such actions do not void the option because she might have other motives.
This is a key distinction: the session condition only applies after the judge formally gives the option.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some narrations (al-Hasan) say separation occurs by her choice alone. The majority (including Abu Yusuf) require a divorce by the husband or a judge's ruling.
The mufta bihi is the majority view.
5
Apply to a scenario
If the wife remarries the husband after separation, she loses her option again because she consented to his condition at the time of remarriage.
This reinforces the principle that consent once given is binding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وإن اختارته بطل حقها) أطلقه فشمل الاختيار حقيقة وحكماً كما إذا قامت من مجلسها أو أقامها أعوان القاضي قبل أن تختار شيئاً أو قام القاضي قبل أن تختار لإمكان أن تختار مع القيام وعليه الفتوى؛ كذا في المحيط والواقعات وفي البدائع ظاهر الرواية أنه لا يتوقف على المجلس. وقيد بقوله بانت بالتفريق لأن الفرقة لا تقع باختيارها نفسها بل لا بد من تطليق الزوج بائنة أو تفريق القاضي إن امتنع وقيل تقع باختيارها وجعله في الخلاصة ظاهر الرواية والأول رواية الحسن. وأشار ببطلانه باختيارها إلى أنه لو فرق بينهما ثم تزوجها ثانياً لم يكن لها خيار لرضاها بحاله كما لو تزوجته عالمة بحاله على المفتى به كما في المحيط. وفي قوله : (لما قررنا أن التخيير شامل لهما الخ قال في النهر : أنت خبير بأن الإتيان بالفاء بعد قوله وأجل سنة ينبو عنه وكان المصنف استغنى بذكر الانتهاء عن الابتداء لاتحاد الحال فيهما قوله : أصغر بيضة الدجاجة) في البدائع : بيضة الديك وفي بعض الكتب بيضة الحمامة قوله : (لم يسعها أن تتزوج بآخر الخ) وجهه بطلان التفريق لكونه في نفس الأمر وطئها؛ كذا في حواشي مسكين. فالمراد أنه لا يسعها ديانة لعلمها بعدم صحة التفريق في نفس الأمر قوله : (كما إذا قامت من مجلسها الخ) أقول: لا يقال إن هذا مخالف لما قدمه من أن طلب التفريق غير مقيد بالحال حتى لو أقامت زماناً وهو يضاجعها فهي على خيارها لأنا نقول ذاك فيما إذا لم يخيرها القاضي أما إذا خيرها فهو على الفور ولذا قال في البدائع : ما يبطل به الخيار نوعان : نص ودلالة فالنص هو التصريح بإسقاط الخيار أو ما يجري مجراه سواء كان ذلك بعد تخيير القاضي أو قبله والدلالة أن تفعل ما يدل على الرضا بالمقام معه فإن خيرها القاضي فأقامت معه مطاوعة في المضاجعة وغير ذلك كان دليل الرضا به, ولو فعلت ذلك بعد مضي الأجل قبل تخيير القاضي لم يكن ذلك رضاً لأنه قد يكون لاختياره وقد يكون لاختيار حاله فلا يكون رضاً مع الاحتمال وهل يبطل خيارها بالقيام عن المجلس؟ فذكر الكرخي عن أبي يوسف أنه إذا خيرها الحاكم فأقامت معه أو قامت عن مجلسها قبل أن تختار أو قام . الحاكم أو أقامها عن مجلسها أعوانه ولم تقل شيئاً فلا خيار لها. وذكر القاضي في شرحه مختصر
His statement: (If she chooses him, her right is void) is absolute, including choice in reality and legally, such as if she stands up from her session, or the judge's assistants make her stand before she chooses anything, or the judge stands before she chooses, because it is possible for her to choose while standing; and upon this is the fatwa. Similarly in al-Muhit and al-Waqi'at. In al-Bada'i', the apparent narration is that it does not depend on the session. And he restricted by saying 'she becomes separated by separation' because the separation does not occur by her own choice, rather the husband must give a final divorce or the judge must separate if he refuses. It is also said that it occurs by her choice, and in al-Khulasah he made that the apparent narration, and the first is the narration of al-Hasan. And he indicated by its voidance by her choice that if he separates them then marries her again, she has no option due to her consent to his condition, like if she marries him knowing his condition according to the mufta bihi, as in al-Muhit. In his statement: (Since we established that the option includes both) he said in al-Nahr: You know that the introduction of fa' after his saying 'and he defer a year' is incompatible, and the author dispensed with mentioning the beginning by mentioning the end because the situation is the same in both. His statement: (the smallest egg of a chicken) in al-Bada'i': a rooster's egg, and in some books a pigeon's egg. His statement: (she is not permitted to marry another) its basis is the invalidity of the separation because in reality he had intercourse with her; similarly in Hawashi Miskin. So the meaning is that she is not permitted in conscience because she knows the separation is invalid in reality. His statement: (like when she stands up from her session) I say: It is not said that this contradicts what he previously stated that the request for separation is not restricted to the moment, even if she stays for a time while he lies with her, she is still had her option. We say that is when the judge has not given her an option, but when he does, it is immediate. Hence in al-Bada'i': What voids the option are two types: text and indication. Text is the explicit dropping of the option or what takes its place, whether after the judge's option or before. Indication is her doing something indicating consent to stay with him. If the judge gives her the option and she stays with him complying in lying together etc., that is evidence of consent. If she does that after the period has passed before the judge's option, it is not consent because she might be doing it for her choice or for her situation, so it is not consent with possibility. Does her standing up from the session void her option? Al-Karkhi reported from Abu Yusuf that if the judge gives her the option and she stays with him or stands up from her session before choosing, or the judge stands, or his assistants make her stand and she says nothing, she has no option. And al-Qadi mentioned in his commentary on Mukhtasar...
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage explains the commentator's clarification of the matn's phrase regarding the wife's choice. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the effect of the wife choosing to stay (ikhtaratuhu). The ruling is that if she chooses to stay, her right to demand separation falls. This applies whether she explicitly chooses or implicitly indicates consent, such as by standing up from the session where she was given the option. The Hanafi position holds that the separation itself requires a divorce by the husband or a judge's ruling; it does not occur by her mere choice. However, there is a narration from al-Hasan that it does occur by her choice. The mufta bihi is that standing from the session without opting voids her option, as per Abu Yusuf. The text distinguishes between being given the option by the judge (when it is immediate) and before that (when it is not immediate). The key point is that any action indicating consent, such as staying with him complying in intercourse, voids her option. If she does such actions after the deferment period but before the judge gives the option, it is not considered consent because she might have other reasons. The passage also clarifies that if the couple separates and then remarries, she loses her option because she consented to his condition. The method of determining virginity using chicken eggs is also mentioned, with difference in the type of egg.

Key Terms
المَجلِس (al-majlis): The session in which the judge presents the option to the wife; her action in that session (e.g., standing) constitutes an implicit choice.
الاِختِيار (al-ikhtiyar): The wife's choice to stay with the husband after being given the option to separate; this voids her right.
البَوَاء (al-bawwal): Method of testing virginity by urinating on a wall; if urine reaches the wall, she is a virgin; otherwise not.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Her option is voided because standing implies consent.
C) She must sit down again to choose.
D) The judge cancels the option.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the wife's option is voided by any explicit or implicit indication of consent, especially in the session where the option is given, and separation requires a separate act by the husband or judge.

Methods to Determine Virginity and Ruling on Her Claim
Explains physical tests and ruling on wife's claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the physical tests described in the Hanafi texts for determining virginity and apply the ruling when a wife claims loss of hymen from other causes.

Core Idea
A wife's claim that her hymen was removed by non-intercourse causes is accepted because the original state is presumed.

This passage from the commentary explains practical methods used historically to assess virginity, and then addresses a crucial legal scenario: when a wife is found to be a non-virgin but attributes it to something other than intercourse. The Hanafi ruling prioritizes the wife's claim based on the principle of istishab (presumption of continuity). These tests are indicative, not legally binding, and the ruling protects the wife's integrity in the absence of evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the physical tests
Note the three methods: urinating on a wall, inserting egg content, or a small chicken egg. Understand these are folk methods, not shar'i evidence.
These tests are mentioned in Hanafi texts but are not considered definitive legal proofs.
2
Understand the legal scenario
The wife is found to be a non-virgin (thayyib) and claims the hymen was removed by something other than sexual intercourse, e.g., her husband's finger or an accident.
The husband might suspect previous intercourse, but the wife offers an alternative cause.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle
The husband's statement is not automatically accepted. Instead, the wife's claim is taken because the apparent (zahir) supports her: the original state is that any hymen loss is not due to illicit intercourse, and the principle (asl) is absence of other causes.
This relies on istishab al-hal (presumption of continuity) and the maxim 'al-asl 'adam al-asbab'.
4
Note the authorities
The passage cites al-Bada'i, al-Isbijabi, al-Kafi, al-Khaniyya, and al-Mi'raj as sources for these rulings. Recognize that later Hanafi works often repeat and rely on these.
This shows the chain of transmission and authority in the Hanafi school.
5
Recognize the practical outcome
If the wife's claim is accepted, the marriage is considered valid and no further action is taken against her. The husband cannot accuse her of fornication without proof.
This protects the wife's honor and legal status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المفيد للجماع اتفاقي أو لبيان الأولى للاكتفاء بقول الواحدة والاثنتان أحوط، وفي البدائع أوثق، وفي الاسبيجابي أفضل وشرط الحاكم الشهيد في الكافي عدالتها. وطريق معرفة أنها بكر أن تبول على جدار فإن وصل إليه فبكر وإلا فلا أو يرسل في فرجها ما في بيضة فإن دخل فثيب وإلا فبكر، أو يرسل في فرجها أصغر بيضة للدجاجة فإن دخلت من غير عنف فهي ثيب وإلا فبكر. وفي الخانية وإن شهد البعض بالبكارة والبعض بالثيابة يريها غيرهن اهـ. وفي المعراج : لو وجدت ثيباً وزعمت أن عذرتها زالت بسبب أخر من غير وطئه كأصبعه وغيرها فالقول قوله لأنه الظاهر والأصل عدم أسباب أخر.
What is beneficial for intercourse is accidental or for clarification: it is better to suffice with the statement of one or two, and two are more precautionary. In al-Bada'i, it is more reliable; in al-Isbijabi, it is better; and al-Hakim al-Shahid in al-Kafi stipulated her (the witness) integrity. And the way to know that she is a virgin is that she urinates on a wall: if it reaches it, she is a virgin; otherwise no. Or one sends into her vagina what is in an egg; if it enters, she is a non-virgin; otherwise a virgin. Or one sends into her vagina the smallest chicken egg; if it enters without force, she is a non-virgin; otherwise a virgin. In al-Khaniyya: if some witness to virginity and others to non-virginity, she is shown to others. In al-Mi'raj: if a woman is found to be a non-virgin and claims that her hymen was removed by a cause other than intercourse, like his finger or other, then his statement is taken because it is the apparent and the principle is absence of other causes.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage from the commentary explains the practical methods to determine whether a woman is a virgin (bikr) or not (thayyib). The author first notes different opinions on how many witnesses suffice, with two being precautionary. Then he describes three physical tests: (1) urinating on a wall to see if the stream reaches it (a folk method, not legal), (2) inserting something like an egg's content, (3) inserting a small chicken egg without force. These are meant as practical indicators, not legal proofs. Then he presents a ruling: if a wife is found to be a non-virgin but claims her hymen was removed by something other than intercourse (like her husband's finger or any other cause), her claim is accepted because the original state (lack of non-marital intercourse) is assumed. This is a Hanafi position based on external appearance and the principle of 'istishab al-asl' (presumption of continuity). The text refers to various Hanafi sources like al-Bada'i, al-Isbijabi, al-Kafi, al-Khaniyya, and al-Mi'raj.

Key Terms
بكر (bikr): A woman who has never had sexual intercourse, i.e., a virgin.
ثيب (thayyib): A woman who has had sexual intercourse, non-virgin.
عذرة (ʿudhra): Hymen membrane; its removal indicates previous intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Her claim is rejected because the apparent proves intercourse.

C) The husband's statement is taken because he has more knowledge.
D) The judge must investigate further with witnesses.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when a wife claims loss of virginity from other causes, her word is accepted because the original state (istishab) presumes no illicit cause.

The Impotent Husband: When Truth Contradicts the Judge's Decree
Ruling on a previously impotent husband who had intercourse but wife claims he did not after a year.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling concerning a wife who denies her husband's intercourse after a judge's separation, and distinguish between the outward legal effect (qada) and the inner reality (diyana).

Core Idea
A judge's decree based on falsehood binds outwardly, but the knowing party must not exploit it.

Impotence (inanah) gives the wife an option to seek annulment after a year-long deadline set by the judge. But what if the husband proves potency during that year, yet the wife later denies it? This lesson unpacks a nuanced ruling from al-Muhit that highlights the delicate balance between judicial authority and individual moral responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Read the case carefully: an impotent husband (aneen), a non-virgin wife (thayyib), a judge-given year, intercourse during the year, and the wife's claim after the year that he did not have intercourse.
Thayyib is irrelevant to the core dispute here, but it signals that the wife was not a virgin at the time of marriage.
2
Trace the Legal Process
The judge set a one-year deadline. During that year, the husband had intercourse. After the year, the wife claimed he did not and demanded he swear an oath. He refused, so the judge separated them.
The wife's demand for an oath indicates she wants a legal confirmation of his impotence.
3
State the Ruling
The text rules: 'She is not allowed to marry another man, and he is not allowed to marry her sister.' This is the operative ruling of the passage.
The ruling is stated in the passive: 'لم يسعها' (it is not permissible for her) and 'لم يسعه' (it is not permissible for him).
4
Explain the Distinction between Qada and Diyana
Outwardly, the judge's separation is valid, so the husband cannot marry the wife's sister because of the prohibition of marrying sisters of a woman one is legally separated from. Inwardly, the wife knows the truth (the husband did have intercourse), so she cannot remarry because the separation was based on a false claim. This is the classic Hanafi distinction between qada (judicial decree) and diyana (inner religious duty).
The same distinction applies in cases where a woman remarries after a fake divorce – she must not consummate the new marriage knowing the divorce was invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط : عنين أجله القاضي سنة وامرأته ثيب فوطئها وادعت بعد الحول أنه لم يطأها وقالت حلفه فأبى أن يحلف ففرق القاضي بينهما لم يسعها أن تتزوج بآخر ولم يسعه أن بأختها اهـ.
And in al-Muhit: An impotent man (aneen) was given a year's deadline by the judge, and his wife was a non-virgin (thayyib). He then had intercourse with her. After the year, she claimed he did not have intercourse and said, 'Make him swear,' but he refused to swear. So the judge separated them. She is not allowed to marry another man, and he is not allowed to marry her sister.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage from al-Muhit presents a specific case: an impotent husband who was granted a year's deadline. During that year, he had intercourse with his wife (she was already thayyib). After the year elapsed, the wife claimed he did not have intercourse (i.e., he did not fulfill the requirement) and demanded he take an oath. When he refused, the judge separated them. The ruling: The wife cannot marry another man (because she knows the separation was invalid in reality since he did have intercourse), and the husband cannot marry her sister (because the separation is still legally effective outwardly). This highlights the distinction between outward legal effects and inner reality (diyana vs. qada). The wife, knowing the truth, must not act on an invalid separation.

Key Terms
عنين (ʿanīn): A man who is impotent, unable to perform sexual intercourse due to a permanent defect.
أجل سنة (ajal sanah): A one-year period set by the judge for the husband to prove he can have intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of an impotent husband who had intercourse during the year, but after the year the wife swore he did not, what is the ruling on her remarriage?
A) She may remarry immediately because the judge separated them.
B) She cannot remarry because she knows the separation was invalid in reality.
C) She must wait for a new court order.
D) She can remarry if the husband agrees.

Key Takeaway
The wife who knows the judge's separation was based on falsehood must not remarry, while the husband cannot marry her sister due to the outwardly valid decree.

When the Wife's Standing After Judge's Offer Voids Her Option: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on voiding wife's option by standing up.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the wife's option is void when she stands up after the judge's offer, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and other narrations.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, the wife's option in impotence is void by any action indicating satisfaction, such as standing up after the judge's offer.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the precise moment when the wife loses her right to demand annulment due to her husband's impotence. The judge offers her a choice; if she stands up without choosing, does she lose her option? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute, with the relied-upon position being that standing up voids it. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this ruling and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Context
Recognize the scenario: a wife whose husband is impotent has the option to seek annulment. The judge must offer her a choice (takhīr) to stay or leave.
This offer is a prerequisite for annulment in Hanafi law.
2
Identify Actions That Void
Classify the two ways the option can be lost: explicit waiver (text) and actions indicating satisfaction (indication). Examples of indication include staying with him willingly or standing up from the session.
The passage focuses on standing up as a key indicative action.
3
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Note the differing views: Abu Yusuf holds that standing up voids the option immediately. Al-Qadi states that the option is not restricted to the session. The fatwa follows Abu Yusuf.
This dispute is based on interpreting the wife's intention.
4
Apply the Mufta Bihi
The operative ruling: if the wife stands up after the judge's offer without choosing, her option is void. She cannot later demand annulment. This is based on the principle of immediacy (fawriyya).
The same applies if she stays with him compliantly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإن يتزوج اختارته بطل حقها أطلقه فشمل الاختيار حقيقة وحكماً كما إذا قامت من مجلسها أو أقامها أعوان القاضي قبل أن تختار شيئاً أو قام القاضي قبل أن تختار لإمكان أن تختار مع القيام وعليه الفتوى؛ كذا في المحيط والواقعات وفي البدائع ظاهر الرواية أنه لا يتوقف على المجلس. وقيد بقوله بانت بالتفريق لأن الفرقة لا تقع باختيارها نفسها بل لا بد من تطليق الزوج بائنة أو تفريق القاضي إن امتنع وقيل تقع باختيارها وجعله في الخلاصة ظاهر الرواية والأول رواية الحسن. وأشار ببطلانه باختيارها إلى أنه لو فرق بينهما ثم تزوجها ثانياً لم يكن لها خيار لرضاها بحاله كما لو تزوجته عالمة بحاله على المفتى به كما في المحيط. وفي البدائع : ما يبطل به الخيار نوعان : نص ودلالة فالنص هو التصريح بإسقاط الخيار أو ما يجري مجراه سواء كان ذلك بعد تخيير القاضي أو قبله والدلالة أن تفعل ما يدل على الرضا بالمقام معه فإن خيرها القاضي فأقامت معه مطاوعة في المضاجعة وغير ذلك كان دليل الرضا به، ولو فعلت ذلك بعد مضي الأجل قبل تخيير القاضي لم يكن ذلك رضاً لأنه قد يكون لاختياره وقد يكون لاختيار حاله فلا يكون رضاً مع الاحتمال وهل يبطل خيارها بالقيام عن المجلس؟ فذكر الكرخي عن أبي يوسف أنه إذا خيرها الحاكم فأقامت معه أو قامت عن مجلسها قبل أن تختار أو قام الحاكم أو أقامها عن مجلسها أعوانه ولم تقل شيئاً فلا خيار لها. وذكر القاضي في شرحه مختصر الطحاوي أنه لا يقتصر على المجلس في ظاهر الرواية.
His statement: (And if she marries one who chooses her, her right is void). He made it absolute, so it includes choice in reality and legally, like if she stands up from her session or the judge's assistants make her stand before she chooses anything, or the judge stands before she chooses, because it is possible for her to choose while standing. And upon this is the fatwa; likewise in al-Muhit and al-Waqi'at, and in al-Bada'i the apparent narration is that it does not depend on the session. And he restricted by his saying 'she becomes separated by separation' because the separation does not occur by her own choice; rather, it requires the husband's irrevocable divorce or the judge's separation if he refuses. And it was said that it occurs by her choice, and al-Khulasa made that the apparent narration, while the first is the narration of al-Hasan. And he indicated by 'its voidance by her choice' that if he separates between them and then he marries her again, she has no option due to her satisfaction with his condition, just as if she married him knowing his condition, according to the mufta bihi, as in al-Muhit. And in al-Bada'i: what voids the option is two types: text and indication. Text is explicit dropping of option or what is like it, whether after the judge's offer or before. Indication is when she does something indicating satisfaction with staying with him. If the judge offers her the choice and she stays with him willingly in intimacy and otherwise, that is evidence of satisfaction. If she does that after the deadline before the judge's offer, it is not satisfaction because it could be due to her own choice or due to choice of his condition, so it is not satisfaction with probability. And does her option become void by standing up from the session? Al-Karkhi reported from Abu Yusuf that if the judge offers her the choice and she stays with him or stands from her session before choosing, or the judge stands or his assistants make her stand from her session and she says nothing, then she has no option. And al-Qadi in his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Tahawi said that it is not restricted to the session in the apparent narration.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the ruling that if a wife marries another who is chosen, her option becomes void. The author explains that 'choice' includes actual and legal scenarios, such as standing up from the session. The fatwa is that the option becomes immediate once offered by the judge. The author clarifies that separation does not happen by the wife's own selection; rather, the husband must pronounce a ba'in divorce or the judge separates if the husband refuses. There is a dispute: the narration in al-Khulasa says her choice itself effects separation, but the preferred view is from al-Hasan's narration (i.e., separation requires official act). Then the author explains that if the wife remarries the same husband after separation, she loses her option because she has shown satisfaction with his condition. This is analogous to marrying him while knowing his impotence. The passage then presents a classification from al-Bada'i: loss of option occurs by explicit text (saying she drops it) or by indication (actions showing satisfaction). Importantly, actions after the judge's offer indicate satisfaction, but similar actions before the offer are ambiguous. Finally, there is a discussion on standing up: according to Abu Yusuf, if she stands up without choosing, she loses her option; but according to some, it is not restricted to the session.

Key Terms
تخيير (takhīr): The act of the judge offering the wife a choice between staying with her impotent husband or seeking annulment.
فورية (fawriyya): Immediacy; the option must be exercised immediately, not deferred.
رضا (riḍā): Satisfaction; actions indicating the wife's willingness to remain in the marriage, thus forfeiting the option.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the favored Hanafi view, what is the effect if the wife stands up from her session after the judge offers her the choice?
A) She retains her option and can choose later.
B) Her option becomes void immediately.
C) She must be asked again by the judge.
D) The husband must divorce her.

Key Takeaway
The wife's option is void by actions indicating satisfaction, such as standing up after the judge's offer, according to the Hanafi mufta bihi.

Counting the Year: What Counts and What Does Not
Basic rule on counting the year for impotence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which periods are counted toward the one-year deadline for the impotent husband and which are not, according to the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Menstruation, Ramadan, Hajj, and absence count; illness of either spouse does not.

The Hanafi school imposes a one-year deadline for the impotent husband before the wife can seek annulment. However, the calculation of this year is not a simple calendar count. Certain events automatically count toward the year, while others pause it. This lesson covers the basic rule and its main exceptions as established in the later fatwa works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The text begins with 'ويحتسب من السنة' meaning certain periods are counted from the year.
2
List what counts
Days of menstruation, Ramadan, the husband's Hajj, and his absence are counted.
These are periods when intercourse is affected or the husband is absent.
3
Identify what does not count
The illness of either spouse does not count, and this is the mufta bihi absolutely.
Illness is a legitimate excuse that extends the deadline.
4
Understand the authority
The ruling is based on al-Walwaljiyya, indicating reliance on later Hanafi fatwa collections.
This is a fatawa mutakhkhirin source.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويحتسب من السنة أيام حيضها ورمضان وحجه وغيبته لا بمرض أحدهما على المفتى به مطلقاً كما في الولوالجية. وصحح في الخانية أن الشهر لا يحتسب وما دونه يحتسب. وفي المحيط أصح الروايات عن أبي يوسف أن نصف الشهر وما دونه يحتسب وما زاد على النصف لا يحتسب ولا بحجها وغيبتها وحبسها وامتناعها من المجيء إلى السجن بعد حبسه بعد أن يكون فيه موضع خلوة ولو على مهرها وفي الخلاصة : لو كان محرماً وقت الخصومة أجله بعد الإحرام. وفي الخانية : لو وجدت زوجها مريضاً لا يقدر على الجماع لا يؤجل ما لم يصح وإن طال المرض اهـ وفيها وإن كان الزوج مظاهراً منها إن كان قادراً على الإعتاق أجله القاضي، وإن كان عاجزاً عنه أمهله القاضي شهرين للكفارة ثم يؤجل، وإن ظاهر بعد التأجيل لا يلتفت إليه ويحتسب ذلك عليه .اهـ.
And from the year are counted: the days of her menstruation, Ramadan, his Hajj, and his absence. Not counted is the illness of either spouse, according to the mufta bihi absolutely, as in al-Walwaljiyya. And it is corrected in al-Khaniyya that a month is not counted, but less than a month is counted. And in al-Muhit, the most authentic narration from Abu Yusuf is that half a month or less is counted, and more than half is not counted. Nor are counted her Hajj, her absence, her imprisonment, and her refusal to come to the prison after his imprisonment, provided that there is a place of seclusion, even if it be for her dower. And in al-Khulasa: if he was in ihram at the time of litigation, his deadline is after ihram. And in al-Khaniyya: if she finds her husband sick, unable to have intercourse, he is not given a deadline until he recovers, even if the sickness is prolonged. And in it: if the husband has made zihar from her, if he is capable of manumission, the judge gives him a deadline; if he is incapable, the judge gives him two months for kaffarah, then he gives a deadline. And if he makes zihar after the deadline, no attention is paid to it, and it is accounted against him.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage discusses the calculation of the one-year deadline for the impotent husband. Key points: (1) Days of menstruation, Ramadan fasting, Hajj, and the husband's absence are counted as part of the year. (2) Illness of either spouse does not count (the year is extended if one is ill). (3) There is a dispute about whether a full month of absence counts: in al-Khaniyya, a month does not count, but less than a month does. Al-Muhit reports from Abu Yusuf that half a month or less counts, more than half does not. (4) The wife's own Hajj, absence, or imprisonment do not count against the husband unless there is a place of seclusion. (5) Special cases: if the husband is in ihram, the deadline starts after ihram. If the husband is sick and cannot have intercourse, no deadline is set until he recovers. If the husband has performed zihar (a form of divorce), he is given a deadline: if he can manumit, he does so immediately; if not, two months for kaffarah, then the deadline for impotence. If he makes zihar after the deadline, it is ignored and the previous deadline stands.

Key Terms
احتساب (ihtisāb): Counting certain periods as part of the one-year deadline for the impotent husband.
غيبة (ghayba): The husband's absence; those days count toward the year if he is not present to have intercourse.
حيض (hayd): The wife's menstruation days, which count toward the year.
رمضان (Ramadan): The month of fasting; these days count toward the year.
مرض (marad): Illness of either spouse; does not count toward the year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school, does the illness of the husband count toward the one-year deadline?
A) Yes, it counts because he is absent from intercourse.
B) No, it does not count, and the deadline is extended.
C) Only if the illness is temporary.
D) It is debated; the preferred view is that it counts.

Key Takeaway
Illness of either spouse does not count toward the year, extending the deadline.

Disputes in Counting and Special Cases: Month, Ihram, Sickness, Zihar
Detailed rules and disputes on the year calculation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on counting a full month of absence and apply the special rules for ihram, husband's illness, and zihar.

Core Idea
A full month of absence is disputed; husband's illness delays the start; zihar imposes separate deadlines.

The calculation of the year becomes more nuanced when dealing with a full month of absence, the wife's own obligations (Hajj, imprisonment), and special conditions of the husband such as ihram, illness, or having made zihar. This lesson unpacks these details from the later Hanafi works.

Guided Path
1
Examine the dispute on counting a full month
Al-Khaniyya says a month is not counted; Abu Yusuf says half a month or less counts.
The difference affects periods between half a month and a full month.
2
Identify the ruling for wife's absence and imprisonment
Her Hajj, absence, and imprisonment do not count if there is a place of seclusion.
The condition is that the prison has a private space for the couple.
3
Apply the rule for husband in ihram
If the husband is in ihram at litigation, his deadline starts after ihram.
Ihram prevents intercourse, so the year is postponed.
4
Understand the effect of husband's illness
If the husband is sick and cannot have intercourse, the deadline is postponed until he recovers, even if prolonged.
No deadline is set while he is ill.
5
Handle the case of zihar
If the husband has made zihar, the judge gives him a deadline based on his ability to perform kaffarah.
Zihar adds an independent time requirement before the impotence deadline.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And from the year are counted: the days of her menstruation, Ramadan, his Hajj, and his absence. Not counted is the illness of either spouse, according to the mufta bihi absolutely, as in al-Walwaljiyya. And it is corrected in al-Khaniyya that a month is not counted, but less than a month is counted. Commentary
This passage discusses the calculation of the one-year deadline for the impotent husband. Key points: (1) Days of menstruation, Ramadan fasting, Hajj, and the husband's absence are counted as part of the year. (2) Illness of either spouse does not count (the year is extended if one is ill). (3) There is a dispute about whether a full month of absence counts: in al-Khaniyya, a month does not count, but less than a month does. Key Terms
شهر (shahr): A month of absence; disputed whether it counts.
إحرام (ihrām): The state of consecration for Hajj/Umrah; during which intercourse is prohibited.
مرض (marad): Sickness preventing intercourse; postpones the deadline indefinitely.
ظهار (zihār): A pronouncement likening the wife to a prohibited relative; requires kaffarah.
خلوة (khalwa): Seclusion; a private space where the couple can be alone.

Wali as Representative in Disputes
Principle: wali can be litigant where agency valid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for when a wali can represent a wife in a separation case and identify which types of separation allow agency.

Core Idea
A wali can represent his ward only where agency is valid; where agency is invalid, the wali cannot intervene.

This passage from al-Muhit al-Jami' of Imam al-Sarakhsi lays out a foundational principle: the legal representative (wali) of a wife can step into a marital dispute only in matters where agency (wakala) is permitted. This distinction determines many practical rulings in Hanafi family law. We will unpack the rule and its applications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the pivot
The passage states: 'every place where agency is valid, the wali becomes a litigant.' So the key is whether wakala is allowed in that specific type of case.
Agency means delegating one's legal action to another.
2
List the allowed cases
From the text: separation due to castration (jabb), option of puberty (khiyar al-bulugh), and lack of competency (kafa'a). In these, the wali can act.
These are cases where the wife has a right to seek annulment and can authorize someone.
3
List the disallowed cases
Separation due to refusal to accept Islam (iba' 'an al-Islam) and li'an (mutual cursing) are excluded. In these, the wife must act personally or through court directly.
Li'an requires personal oaths; refusal to accept Islam is a personal status change.
4
Explain the underlying reason
Agency is not valid where the action requires personal participation (like oath-taking in li'an) or where the cause is based on personal belief (like apostasy). The wali cannot deputize in matters that are inherently personal.
This is based on Hanafi rulings on wakala.
5
Apply the rule
Given a new scenario—husband is impotent? Can wali act? Yes, because impotence is similar to castration. Husband disappears? The wali may seek divorce only if agency is allowed in such cases.
Impotence falls under jabb (castration) by extension.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط الجامع : أصله أن كل موضع تجري الوكالة فيه ينتصب الولي فيه خصماً فالتفريق بسبب الجب وخيار البلوغ وعدم الكفاءة تجري الوكالة فيه فانتصب الولي فيه خصماً، وكل موضع لا تجري الوكالة فيه لا ينتصب الولي خصماً فيه كالفرقة بالإباء عن الإسلام واللعان اهـ.
And in al-Muhit al-Jami': Its principle is that every place where agency (wakala) is valid, the guardian (wali) becomes a litigant. So separation due to castration, option of puberty, and lack of competency – agency is valid in them, thus the guardian becomes a litigant. And every place where agency is not valid, the guardian does not become a litigant, like separation due to refusal to accept Islam and li'an.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage from al-Muhit al-Jami' establishes a principle: the guardian (wali) of a wife can represent her in court in cases where agency (wakala) is allowed. This applies to separations based on the husband's castration (jabb), the wife's option of puberty (khiyar al-bulugh), and lack of marital competence (kafa'a). In all these, the wali can act on behalf of the wife. However, in cases where agency is not valid, such as separation due to the husband's refusal to accept Islam (iba' 'an al-Islam) or li'an (mutual cursing), the wali cannot be a litigant; the wife must appear personally or the matter is handled differently. This is because agency is not allowed in matters that require personal participation (like divorce or li'an).

Key Terms
ولي (walī): Guardian, usually the wife's father or next male relative, who can represent her in marriage and some legal matters.
وكالة (wakāla): Agency; the delegation of legal authority to another to act on one's behalf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which of the following separations can the wali NOT act as a litigant?
A) Separation due to castration (jabb).
B) Separation due to option of puberty (khiyar al-bulugh).
C) Separation due to lack of competency (kafa'a).
D) Separation due to li'an.

Key Takeaway
The wali's ability to represent his ward in a marital dispute hinges entirely on whether agency is valid for that type of case.

intermediate
8 min
No Option for Spouse Defects: Qiyas Proof
Defense of Hanafi rule via qiyas from death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar for spousal defects and explain the qiyas argument from death before consummation.

Core Idea
A spousal defect does not annul the marriage because even death does not give an option.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a core Hanafi rule: neither spouse can annul the marriage due to a physical defect in the other. The author defends this with a qiyas (analogy) from death before consummation. We'll walk through the reasoning, the objection raised by other schools, and the Hanafi response to understand why this ruling holds in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the opening statement: 'And neither one is given an option due to a defect.' Recognize this as a negative ruling — no khiyar exists for defects.
The ruling is absolute: applies to both spouses and all defects.
2
Understand the Ratio (Illa)
The text explains why: the right owed is intercourse (wat'), and a defect only causes imperfection, not complete loss. The illa is the partial nature of the loss.
This sets up the qiyas: complete loss (death) vs partial loss (defect).
3
Construct the Qiyas
The qiyas from al-Hidayah is cited: death before consummation does not give an option to annul (marriage ends by death, not rescission). By qiyas auli (stronger analogy), a mere defect is even less deserving of rescission.
Qiyas auli means the ruling in the far' (defect) is even more certain than in the asl (death).
4
Analyze the Objection and Response
Commentators object that marriage is temporary (ends at death), so death is not analogous. The author gives a two-part answer: (1) marriage ends by death (intiha'), not rescission (faskh); ending does not imply option. (2) The second answer is cut off but probably strengthens the distinction.
The response refines the argument: death is a natural termination, not a rescission, so the analogy holds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولم يخير أحدهما بعيب) أي لا خيار لأحد الزوجين بعيب في الآخر لأن المستحق بالعقد هو الوطء والعيب لا يفوته بل يوجب فيه خللاً ففواته بالموت قبل التسليم لا يوجب الخيار فاختلاله أولى وفي الهداية : إن اختلاله بالموت لا يوجب الفسخ فبالعيب أولى. واعترض عليه جميع الشارحين بأن النكاح مؤقت بحياتهما ولم يجيبوا وأجبت عنه بجوابين : الأول أن النكاح ينتهي بالموت لا أنه ينفسخ قالوا والشيء بانتهائه يتقرر ولا
His statement: (And neither one is given an option due to a defect). That is, no option for either spouse due to a defect in the other, because the right owed by the contract is intercourse, and a defect does not eliminate it but causes imperfection in it. So its complete loss by death before consummation does not give an option, so its imperfection is even more deserving. And in al-Hidaya: its imperfection by death does not necessitate rescission, so by defect it is even more deserving. And all the commentators objected to this, saying that marriage is temporary with their lives, and they did not answer. And I answered it with two answers: the first is that marriage ends by death, not that it is rescinded; they said, and a thing by its ending is established, and not...
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage addresses the rule that neither spouse has an option to annul the marriage due to a physical defect (like impotence, leprosy, etc.) in the other spouse. The reasoning: the primary right in marriage is sexual intercourse, and a defect does not remove this right entirely but only causes imperfection. Since complete loss of this right through death before consummation does not give a right to annulment (marriage ends by death, not rescission), then mere imperfection due to a defect is even less deserving of annulment. The author notes that commentators objected, arguing that marriage is temporary (since it ends at death), so analogizing to death is problematic. The author gives two answers, but only the first is complete: marriage ends by death, it is not rescinded; when something ends by its nature, its consequences are appreciated (the marriage remained valid until death). The second answer is cut off. This is a refined argument defending the Hanafi position against objections.

Key Terms
خيار (khiyār): Option to annul the marriage contract due to a defect in the partner.
عيب (ʿayb): A physical defect in a spouse that interferes with the purpose of marriage (e.g., impotence, leprosy).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary proof used in the text to argue that a defect in a spouse does not give an option to annul?
A) A Quranic verse.
B) A hadith.
C) Qiyas on death before consummation.
D) Consensus of the companions.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school denies any option to annul marriage due to a spouse's defect, based on qiyas auli from death before consummation.

The Wife's Option Due to Impotence: The Year-Long Waiting Period
Explaining the legal period and conditions for the wife's option

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the duration of the wife's option in case of an impotent husband and identify which periods are excluded from the count.

Core Idea
The wife's option for annulment begins after one year, counting only days she was available for intercourse.

The Hanafi school grants the wife of an impotent husband ('aneen) the right to seek annulment after one full year of non-consummation. However, not all days are counted equally. This lesson explains the general rule and the key exclusions that protect the wife's right.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Understand that the wife has an option (khiyar) to seek annulment after one year from the time she brings the case to court.
The year is calculated from the date of litigation, not marriage.
2
Identify what is counted
Days when the wife was available for intercourse are counted. If she was unavailable due to menstruation, Ramadan fasting, Hajj, or husband's absence, those days are excluded.
The text explicitly mentions these exclusions.
3
Note the effect of illness
Illness of either spouse does not cause exclusion according to the relied-upon fatwa.
Contrary to some views, illness is not a valid excuse to stop the clock.
4
Understand the rationale
The exclusions ensure fairness: the wife should not lose her right due to circumstances beyond her control.
The option is a mercy for the wife, not a tool for the husband to delay.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخانية : فرق بين العنين وبين امرأته ثم تزوج أخرى تعلم بحاله اختلفت الروايات والصحيح أن للثانية حق الخصومة لأن الإنسان قد يعجز عن امرأة ولا يعجز عن غيرها. ويحتسب من السنة أيام حيضها ورمضان وحجه وغيبته لا بمرض أحدهما على المفتى به مطلقاً كما في الولوالجية. وصحح في الخانية أن الشهر لا يحتسب وما دونه يحتسب. وفي المحيط أصح الروايات عن أبي يوسف أن نصف الشهر وما دونه يحتسب وما زاد على النصف لا يحتسب ولا بحجها وغيبتها وحبسها وامتناعها من المجيء إلى السجن بعد حبسه بعد أن يكون فيه موضع خلوة ولو على مهرها وفي الخلاصة : لو كان محرماً وقت الخصومة أجله بعد الإحرام. وفي الخانية : لو وجدت زوجها مريضاً لا يقدر على الجماع لا يؤجل ما لم يصح وإن طال المرض اهـ وفيها وإن كان الزوج مظاهراً منها إن كان قادراً على الإعتاق أجله القاضي، ، وإن كان عاجزاً عنه أمهله القاضي شهرين للكفارة ثم يؤجل، وإن ظاهر بعد التأجيل لا يلتفت إليه ويحتسب ذلك عليه .اهـ.
Al-Khaniyya: A separation was made between an impotent man and his wife; then he married another who knew his condition. The narrations differed, and the correct view is that the second wife has the right of litigation because a man may be incapable with one woman but not with another. (From the year) her menstrual days, Ramadan, her Hajj, and his absence are counted, but not due to illness of one of them, according to the fatwa absolutely, as in al-Walwalijiyya. And it is corrected in al-Khaniyya that a month is not counted, and what is less than it is counted. In al-Muhit, the most correct narrations from Abu Yusuf are that half a month and less are counted, and more than half is not counted. Nor (are counted) her Hajj, her absence, her imprisonment, and her refusal to come to the prison after his imprisonment, provided that there is a place of seclusion in it, even if for her mahr. In al-Khulasa: If he was in ihram at the time of litigation, he is given a deadline after the ihram. In al-Khaniyya: If she found her husband sick, unable to have intercourse, he is not given a deadline until he recovers, even if the illness is prolonged. And in it: If the husband has made zihar from her, if he is able to emancipate, the judge gives him a deadline; if he is unable, the judge gives him two months for the kaffara, then gives him a deadline. If he makes zihar after the deadline, it is not considered, and that is counted against him.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the rulings related to an impotent husband ('aneen). It begins by stating the divergence of narrations regarding a second wife who marries an impotent man knowing his condition. The correct view is that she retains the right to litigate for annulment, because impotence may be specific to one woman. The passage then details how the year-long waiting period is counted: days of menstruation, Ramadan, Hajj, and the husband's absence are not counted against the wife, while illness of either spouse is also excluded according to the relied-upon fatwa. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Al-Khaniyya states that a full month is not counted, but less than a month is. In al-Muhit, the most authentic narration from Abu Yusuf holds that half a month or less is counted, but more than half is not. Additionally, the wife's own Hajj, absence, imprisonment, or refusal to come to the prison (if the husband is imprisoned and there is a place for seclusion) are not counted, even if she refuses due to her mahr. The passage also covers special cases: if the husband is in ihram at the time of litigation, the deadline is given after ihram (though some scholars say after halal). If the husband is sick and unable to have intercourse, he is not given a deadline until he recovers. If the husband is a muzahir (has made zihar), the judge gives him a deadline to perform kaffara: if capable, immediate emancipation; if not, two months' fasting; then the deadline for annulment is set. Any zihar after the deadline is disregarded and counted against him.

Key Terms
العنين (al-'aneen): A man who is impotent, unable to have intercourse with women.
الخصومة (al-khusumah): Litigation; the right of the wife to bring a case before a judge to seek annulment due to impotence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT excluded from the one-year count?
A) Menstrual days
B) Ramadan fasting days
C) Illness of the wife
D) Husband's absence

Key Takeaway
The wife of an impotent husband must wait one full year, excluding days of menstruation, Ramadan, Hajj, and husband's absence, before she can exercise her option for annulment.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Counting the Year
Explaining the legal period and conditions for the wife's option

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Abu Yusuf's view and the relied-upon fatwa regarding the counting of a month in the waiting period.

Core Idea
Within the Hanafi school: a full month is not counted, but less than a month is; Abu Yusuf counts half a month or less.

The details of counting the one-year period are subject to intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. This lesson focuses on the specific disagreement about how to treat a month when the husband's absence or other factors occur. Understanding this dispute is crucial for correctly applying the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the point of dispute
When the husband is absent for a part of a month, how is that month counted? The text presents two views.
The dispute is over the threshold: full month vs. half month.
2
State the view of al-Khaniyya (relied-upon)
A full month is not counted; anything less than a full month is counted.
This is the mufta bihi according to al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.
3
State the view of Abu Yusuf
Half a month or less is counted; more than half is not counted.
This is the most authentic narration from Abu Yusuf as per al-Muhit.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if the husband is absent for 20 days, under al-Khaniyya it is counted (since less than a month), but under Abu Yusuf it is not counted (since more than half).
This affects when the year is completed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And in it: If the husband has made zihar from her, if he is able to emancipate, the judge gives him a deadline; if he is unable, the judge gives him two months for the kaffara, then gives him a deadline. المفتى به (al-mufta bihi): The relied-upon opinion that is given in fatwa.

Key Takeaway

Special Circumstances: Ihram, Sickness, and Zihar
Explaining the legal period and conditions for the wife's option

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine how the waiting period is affected when the husband is in ihram, sick, or has made zihar.

Core Idea
Ihram, sickness, and zihar each pause or adjust the waiting period rule for the impotent husband.

The Hanafi school provides detailed rules for special situations that may arise during the wife's waiting period. This lesson covers three such cases: the husband who is in ihram, the husband who is sick and unable to consummate, and the husband who has made zihar. These situations modify the normal waiting period rules and reflect the school's attention to exceptional circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case of ihram
If the husband is in ihram at the time the wife brings her case to court, the judge gives a deadline after the ihram ends.
During ihram, sexual intercourse is prohibited, so the husband cannot be expected to consummate.
2
Identify the case of sickness
If the husband is sick and cannot have intercourse, the deadline is suspended until he recovers, even if the illness is prolonged.
The text says 'يؤجل ما لم يصح' (he is not given a deadline until he recovers).
3
Identify the case of zihar
If the husband has made zihar (declaring his wife like his mother's back), he must first perform kaffarah. If he is able to free a slave, the judge gives a deadline for that; if unable, the judge gives him two months to fast as kaffarah, and only then does the waiting period for impotence start.
Any zihar after the deadline is disregarded and counted against him.
4
Note the common principle
In all cases, the husband is not penalized for factors beyond his control, but the wife's right is preserved by allowing the waiting period to resume when the obstacle is removed.
This shows the Hanafi school's balance between the rights of both spouses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخانية : فرق بين العنين وبين امرأته ثم تزوج أخرى تعلم بحاله اختلفت الروايات والصحيح أن للثانية حق الخصومة لأن الإنسان قد يعجز عن امرأة ولا يعجز عن غيرها. ويحتسب من السنة أيام حيضها ورمضان وحجه وغيبته لا بمرض أحدهما على المفتى به مطلقاً كما في الولوالجية. وصحح في الخانية أن الشهر لا يحتسب وما دونه يحتسب. وفي المحيط أصح الروايات عن أبي يوسف أن نصف الشهر وما دونه يحتسب وما زاد على النصف لا يحتسب ولا بحجها وغيبتها وحبسها وامتناعها من المجيء إلى السجن بعد حبسه بعد أن يكون فيه موضع خلوة ولو على مهرها وفي الخلاصة : لو كان محرماً وقت الخصومة أجله بعد الإحرام. وفي الخانية : لو وجدت زوجها مريضاً لا يقدر على الجماع لا يؤجل ما لم يصح وإن طال المرض اهـ وفيها وإن كان الزوج مظاهراً منها إن كان قادراً على الإعتاق أجله القاضي، ، وإن كان عاجزاً عنه أمهله القاضي شهرين للكفارة ثم يؤجل، وإن ظاهر بعد التأجيل لا يلتفت إليه ويحتسب ذلك عليه .اهـ.

Key Terms
الإحرام (al-ihram): The state of consecration during Hajj or Umrah, during which sexual intercourse is prohibited.
الظهار (al-zihar): A form of divorce where the husband says to his wife 'You are to me like the back of my mother', making her forbidden to him until he performs kaffarah.

Definition and Rukn of 'Idda: Hanafi and Shafi'i Views
Linguistic and legal definition of 'idda with Hanafi and Shafi'i comparison and furu'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'idda, identify its rukn as the prohibitions, and distinguish it from the Shafi'i view, applying these definitions to practical cases like interlocking of 'iddas.

Core Idea
For Hanafis, the rukn of 'idda is the prohibitions, not the act of waiting.

In this lesson, we explore the linguistic and legal definition of 'idda (waiting period) as presented in Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The passage not only defines the term but also delves into a foundational inter-madhhab dispute: what is the true rukn (pillar) of 'idda? Understanding this difference is crucial because it leads to divergent rulings on practical issues such as whether two 'iddas can overlap and whether the period ends without the woman's knowledge. Let's walk through the text step by step.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the linguistic definition
The passage begins by defining 'idda linguistically as tarbus (waiting) and quotes Quranic verses to support this meaning. Note the root meaning of counting or waiting.
The Quranic verses establish the linguistic basis, but the legal definition goes beyond mere semantics.
2
Identify the legal definition and Hanafi rukn
The author specifies that the legal rukn according to the Hanafi school is the prohibitions (hurmat) that become binding on the woman, such as the prohibition of remarriage. The actual act of waiting is only a means to fulfill that prohibition, not the essence.
This is a key doctrinal point: the rukn determines the legal nature of 'idda.
3
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
The text reports that Imam al-Shafi'i considers the rukn to be the act of waiting itself (tarbus). Recognize that this is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different understandings of the underlying evidence.
Both schools agree that waiting is required, but they differ on its essential role.
4
Explore practical consequences (furu')
The passage mentions two branches derived from this difference: (1) interlocking of two 'iddas (تداخل العدتين): Hanafis allow overlap, Shafi'is require separate completion. (2) Whether the 'idda ends without the woman's knowledge: Hanafis say yes, Shafi'is say no. Trace how each ruling follows from the respective definition of rukn.
This shows the thamarah al-khilaf—the practical effect of theoretical disagreement.

Source Text

باب العدة هي تربص يلزم المرأة عند زوال النكاح أو شبهته لزوم انتظار انقضاء مدة والتربص التثبت والانتظار قال الله تعالى فتربصوا حتى [المؤمنون : ٢٥] وقال تعالى يتربص بكم الدوائر [التوبة : ۹۸] وقال تعالى فتربصوا إنا معكم متربصون [التوبة : ٥٢] كذا في البدائع وإنما قدرنا اللزوم لأن التربص فعلها وقد قالوا إن ركنها حرمات أي لزومات كحرمة تزوجها على الغير. ونقلوا عن الشافعي أن ركنها التربص عنده وفرعوا على الاختلاف تداخل العدتين، فعندنا يتداخلان خلافاً له وانقضاؤه بدون علمها عندنا خلافا له وهذا أولى مما في البدائع من جعلها في الشرع عندنا اسماً لأجل ضرب لانقضاء ما بقي من آثار النكاح، وعند الشافعي اسماً لفعل التربص
Chapter of the Waiting Period. It is a waiting period incumbent upon the woman upon the removal of marriage or its semblance. ... They reported from al-Shafi'i that its pillar is the act of waiting. And they branched upon the difference the interlocking of two waiting periods: with us they interlock, contrary to him, and its completion without her knowledge is with us, contrary to him.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage defines 'idda legally as a required period of waiting that becomes obligatory for a woman when marriage ends or is dissolved. The author explains the linguistic root (counting, waiting) and quotes Quranic verses. He then distinguishes the Hanafi and Shafi'i views: for Hanafis, the pillar (rukn) of 'idda is the prohibitions (hurmat) that attach to the woman during this period (e.g., prohibition of remarriage), while for Shafi'i it is the actual act of waiting. A practical consequence is the issue of تداخل العدتين (interlocking of waiting periods): if two separations occur simultaneously, Hanafis hold the two periods overlap, reducing the total, whereas Shafi'i says they must be observed separately.

Key Terms
العدة (al-'idda): The waiting period incumbent upon a woman upon dissolution of marriage.
التربص (al-tarbus): Waiting, staying in place.
ركن (rukn): Pillar, integral element of the act.
تداخل العدتين (tadakhul al-'iddatayn): Interlocking of two waiting periods; Hanafis allow them to run concurrently.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The actual waiting (tarbus)
B) The prohibitions (hurmat) such as prohibition of marriage
C) The passage of three menstrual cycles
D) The divorce pronouncement

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rukn of 'idda is the prohibitions, not the act of waiting, and this leads to distinct rulings on interlocking and knowledge.
